}

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1078250]##Model Group Reference

[#50536467_pgfId-1078251]##A model group reference is a reference to a
model group using the “ref” attribute. A property customization is
allowed on the annotation property of the model group reference. Section
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_30958[See Annotation Restrictions]” contains more
information regarding the annotation element for a model group
reference.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078258]##The customization values must be defined as
specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_55656[See Usage]” and have component
scope. A model group reference is bound to a Java property set or a list
property as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536464_77835[See Content Model
Default Binding]” applying customization overrides as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_81943[See Customization Overrides].”

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1078265]##[#50536467_24088]##ComplexType

[#50536467_pgfId-1078266]##A _<property>_ customization is allowed on
the annotation element of a complex type. The customization values must
be defined as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_55656[See Usage]” and
have component scope. The result of this customization depends upon the
content type of the complex type.

* [#50536467_pgfId-1078270]##If the content type of the content model is
simple content, then the content model must be bound to a property as
specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536464_81433[See Simple Content Binding].”
applying the customization overrides as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_81943[See Customization Overrides].” If
_javaType_ is defined, then the _propertyBaseType_ is defined to be Java
datatype specified in the _"name"_ attribute of the _javaType_ .
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078277]##For all other content types, the content
model must be bound as specified in step 1. of
link:jaxb.htm#50536464_77835[See Content Model Default Binding]”
applying the customization overrides as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_81943[See Customization Overrides]".
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078292]##

== [#50536467_pgfId-1078297]##[#50536467_72052]## _<javaType>_ Declaration

[#50536467_pgfId-1078298]##A _<javaType>_ declaration provides a way to
customize the binding of an XML schema atomic datatype to a Java
datatype, referred to as the target Java datatype. The target Java
datatype can be a Java built-in data type or an application specific
Java datatype. This declaration also provides two additional methods: a
parse method and a print method.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078299]##The parse method converts a lexical
representation of the XML schema datatype into a value of the target
Java datatype. The parse method is invoked by a JAXB provider’s
implementation during unmarshalling.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078300]##The print method converts a value of the
target Java datatype into its lexical representation of the XML schema
datatype. The print method is invoked by a JAXB provider’s
implementation during marshalling.

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078303]##Usage

[#50536467_pgfId-1078304]##<javaType name=" _javaType_ "

{empty}[#50536467_pgfId-1078305]## [ xmlType=" _xmlType_ " ]

{empty}[#50536467_pgfId-1078307]## [ parseMethod="parseMethod" ]

[#50536467_pgfId-1078308]## [ printMethod="printMethod" ]>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078309]##The binding declaration can be used in one of
the following:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1081125]##a _<globalBindings>_ declaration.
* [#50536467_pgfId-1081166]##annotation element of one of the XML schema
elements specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_68898[See Customizable
Schema Elements].”
* [#50536467_pgfId-1081172]##in a <property> declaration. See
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_28399[See <property> Declaration].” This can be
used for customization at the point of reference to a simple type.

[#50536467_pgfId-1081136]##When used in a _<globalBindings>_
declaration, _<javaType>_ defines customization values with global
scope. When used in an annotation element of one of the schema elements
specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_68898[See Customizable Schema
Elements].” the customization values have component scope.

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1078316]##name

[#50536467_pgfId-1084845]##The _javaType_ , if specified, is the Java
datatype to which _xmlType_ is to be bound. Therefore, _javaType_ must
be a legal Java type name, which may include a package prefix. If the
package prefix is not present, then the Java type name must be one of
the Java built-in primitive types [JLS - Java Language Specification,
Second Edition, Section 4.2, “Primitive Types and Values”]. (For
example, “ _int_ ”) or a Java class in the unnamed package. If class
javaType declares a public constructor with following signature,
_javaType(java.lang.String)_ , _parseMethod_ attribute does not need to
be specified.

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1078318]## _xmlType_

[#50536467_pgfId-1078319]##The _xmlType_ , if specified, is the name of
the XML Schema datatype to which _javaType_ is to bound. If specified,
_xmlType_ must be a XML atomic datatype derived from restriction. The
use of the _xmlType_ is further constrained as follows.

[#50536467_pgfId-1084123]##The purpose of the _xmlType_ attribute is to
allow the global customization of a XML schema to Java datatype. Hence
_xmlType_ attribute is required when _<javaType>_ declaration’s parent
is _<globalBindings>_ . If absent, it must result in an invalid
customization as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid
Customizations].” Otherwise, the _xmlType_ attribute must not be present
since the XML datatype is determined from the XML schema element with
which the annotation element containing _<javaType>_ declaration or the
_<baseType>_ (containing the _<javaType>_ ) is associated. If present,
it must result in an invalid customization as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid Customizations].”

[#50536467_pgfId-1078323]##Examples can be found in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_84875[See Example: javaType Customization: Java
Built-in Type]” and link:jaxb.htm#50536467_89898[See Example: javaType
Customization: User Specified Parse Method]”

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1082448]## _parseMethod_

[#50536467_pgfId-1078330]##The parse method if specified, must be
applied during unmarshalling in order to convert a string from the input
document into a value of the target Java datatype. The parse method must
be invoked as follows:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1078331]##The parse method defaults to _new_ provided
_javaType_ is not a Java primitive type such as ( _"int"_ ). If
_javaType_ is a Java primitive type, then this must result in an invalid
customization as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid
Customizations].” Otherwise, the binding compiler must assume that the
target type is a class that defines a constructor as follows:
* [#50536467_pgfId-1081946]## _String_ as the first parameter of the
constructor.

[#50536467_pgfId-1082000]##To apply the conversion to a string it must
generate code that invokes this constructor, passing it the input
string.

* [#50536467_pgfId-1081774]##The parse method may be specified in the
form _ClassName.methodName,_ where the ClassName is a fully qualified
class name that includes the package name. A compiler must assume that
the class _ClassName_ exists and that it defines a static method named
_methodName_ that takes:
* [#50536467_pgfId-1083550]## _String_ as the first argument.

[#50536467_pgfId-1099746]##To apply the conversion to a string it must
generate code that invokes this method, passing it the input string.

* [#50536467_pgfId-1099750]##The parse method may be specified in the
form _methodName_ provided _javaType_ is not a Java primitive type (such
as _"int"_ ). If _javaType_ is Java primitive type, then this must
result in an invalid customization as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid Customizations].” Otherwise,
the binding compiler must assume that _methodName_ is a method in the
class _javaType._ The binding compiler must therefore prefix the
_javaType_ to the _methodName_ and process _javaType._ _methodName_ as
specified in above.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078340]##The string passed to parse method can be any
lexical representation for _xmlType_ as specified in [XSD PART2].

[#50536467_pgfId-1098944]##If parseMethod attribute is not specified,
_xmlType_ is not a primitive or wrapper class and _javaType_ has an
accessible one argument constructor, where the argument is type
_java.lang.String_ , input text is parsed by invoking _new_ with a
_java.lang.String_ parameter.

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1078341]## _printMethod_

[#50536467_pgfId-1078342]##The print method if specified, must be
applied during marshalling in order to convert a value of the target
type into a lexical representation:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1083657]##The print method is specified in the form
_methodName_ provided _javaType_ is not a Java primitive type (such as
_"int"_ ). If _javaType_ is Java primitive type, then this must result
in an invalid customization as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid Customizations].” Otherwise,
the compiler must assume that the target type is a class or an interface
that defines a zero-argument instance method named _methodName_ that
returns a _String_ . To apply the conversion it must generate code to
invoke this method upon an instance of the target Java datatype.
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078344]##If the print method is specified in the
form _ClassName.methodName_ then the compiler must assume that the class
_ClassName_ exists and that it defines a static method named
_methodName_ that returns a string that takes the following:
* [#50536467_pgfId-1082057]##the first parameter is the target Java
datatype.

[#50536467_pgfId-1083615]##To apply the conversion to a string it must
generate code that invokes this method, passing it a value of the target
Java datatype.

[#50536467_pgfId-1081909]##The lexical representation to which the value
of the target type is converted can be any lexical representation for
_xmlType_ as specified in [XSD PART2].

[#50536467_pgfId-1098964]##If _printMethod_ attribute is not specified
and _xmlType_ is not a primitive or wrapper class, _javaType.toString()_
is used as the default print method..

[#50536467_pgfId-1098962]## 

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078350]## _DatatypeConverter_

[#50536467_pgfId-1078351]##Writing customized parse and print methods
can be difficult for a Java programmer. This requires a programmer to
understand the lexical representations of XML schema datatypes. To make
it easier, an interface, _DatatypeConverterInterface,_ and a class
_DatatypeConverter_ are defined to expose the parse and print methods of
a JAXB implementation. These can be invoked by user defined parse and
print methods. This shifts the burden of dealing with lexical spaces
back to the JAXB implementation.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078352]##The _DatatypeConverterInterface_ defines
parse and print methods for XML schema datatypes. There is one parse and
print method for each of XML schema datatype specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536464_60588[See Java Mapping for XML Schema Built-in
Types]. The interface is fully specified by the Javadoc specified in
_javax.xml.bind.DatatypeConverterInterface_ .

[#50536467_pgfId-1084187]##The _DatatypeConverter_ class defines a
static parse and print method corresponding to each parse and print
method respectively in the _DatatypeConverterInterface_ interface. The
property _javax.xml.bind.DatatypeConverter_ can be used to select the
name of a class that provides an implementation of the parse and print
methods. The name specified in the property must be a fully qualified
class name and must implement the interface _DatatypeConverterInterface_
. The class is fully specified by the Javadoc specified in
_javax.xml.bind.DatatypeConverter_ .

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1084188]##Usage

[#50536467_pgfId-1081210]##The following example demonstrates the use of
the _DatatypeConverter_ class for writing a customized parse and print
method.

====== [#50536467_pgfId-1082085]##[#50536467_89898]##Example: javaType Customization: User Specified Parse Method

[#50536467_pgfId-1081466]##This example shows the binding of XML schema
type _"xs:date"_ is bound to a Java datatype _long_ using user specified
print and parse methods.

[#50536467_pgfId-1081526]##<jaxb:globalBindings> +
<jaxb:javaType name="long" xmlType="xs:date" +
parseMethod="pkg.MyDatatypeConverter.myParseDate" +
printMethod="pkg.MyDatatypeConverter.myPrintDate"/> +
</jaxb:javaType> +
</jaxb:globalBindings> +

[#50536467_pgfId-1081530]##package pkg; +
import javax.xml.bind.DatatypeConverter;

[#50536467_pgfId-1093469]##public class MyDatatypeConverter \{ +
public static long myParseDate(String s) \{

[#50536467_pgfId-1081531]## java.util.Calendar d =
DatatypeConverter.parse(s);

[#50536467_pgfId-1081532]## long result= cvtCalendarToLong(d) ; // user
defined method

[#50536467_pgfId-1081533]## return result; +
}

[#50536467_pgfId-1084375]## public static String myPrintDate(long l) \{

[#50536467_pgfId-1084376]## java.util.Calendar d = cvtLongToCalendar(l);
//user defined

[#50536467_pgfId-1084377]## return DatatypeConverter.print(d);

[#50536467_pgfId-1081552]## } +
}

[#50536467_pgfId-1081480]##The implementation of the print methods (
_parseDate_ and _printDate_ ) are provided by the user.

[#50536467_pgfId-1081463]##The customization is applied during the
processing of XML instance document. During unmarshalling, the JAXB
implementation invokes _myParseDate_ . If _myParseDate_ method throws a
_ParseException_ , then the JAXB implementation code catches the
exception, and generate a _parseConversionEvent_ .

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1078370]##Lexical And Value Space

[#50536467_pgfId-1078371]##[XSD PART 2] specifies both a value space and
a lexical space for an schema datatypes. There can be more than one
lexical representation for a given value.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078372]##Examples of multiple lexical representations
for a single value are:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1078373]##For boolean, the value _true_ has two
lexical representations _"true"_ and _"1"._
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078374]##For integer, the value _1_ has two lexical
representations _"1.0"_ and _"1"._

[#50536467_pgfId-1078375]##XSD PART 2 also specifies a canonical
representation for all XML schema atomic datatypes.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078376]##The requirements on the parse and print
methods are as follows:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1078377]##A JAXB implementation of a parse method in
_DatatypeConverterInterface_ must be capable of a processing all lexical
representations for a value as specified by [XSD PART 2]. This ensures
that an instance document containing a value in any lexical
representation specified by [XSD PART 2] can be marshalled.
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078378]##A JAXB implementation of a print method in
_DatatypeConverterInterface_ must convert a value into any lexical
representation of the XML schema datatype to which the parse method
applies, as specified by [XSD PART 2] and which is valid with respect to
the application’s schema.
* [#50536467_pgfId-1084206]##

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1084208]##Built-in Conversions

[#50536467_pgfId-1078504]##As a convenience to the user, this section
specifies some built-in conversions. A built-in conversion is one where
the parse and the print method may be omitted by a user. The built-in
conversions leverage the narrowing and widening conversions defined in
[JLS - Java Language Specification, Second Edition], Section 5.1.2,
“Widening Primitive Conversion” and Section 5.1.3, “Narrowing Primitive
Conversions.” For example:

[#50536467_pgfId-1078505]##<xs:simpleType name="foo" type="xs:long">

[#50536467_pgfId-1078506]## <xs:annotation><xs:appinfo>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078507]## <jaxb:javaType name="int"/>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078508]## </xs:appinfo></xs:annotation>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078509]##</xs:simpleType>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078510]##If the parse method is omitted, then a JAXB
implementation must perform the one of the following binding options:

. [#50536467_pgfId-1091664]##If _javaType_ is one of the following
primitive types or its corresponding wrapper class _byte, short, int,
long, float, double_ , bind _xmlType_ to its default Java datatype using
the parse method for the _xmlType_ defined in _DatatypeConverter_ . If
necessary, convert the default Java datatype for _xmlType_ to value of
type _javaType_ by a type cast.
. [#50536467_pgfId-1091672]##Else if default Java datatype defines a
public one-argument constructor that takes a _java.lang.String_ , use
_new_ with a _java.lang.String_ parameter for parsing.
. [#50536467_pgfId-1091679]##Else javaType(java.lang.String) does not
exist, this must result in an invalid binding customization as specified
in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid Customizations].

====== [#50536467_pgfId-1081629]##[#50536467_84875]##Example: javaType Customization: Java Built-in Type

[#50536467_pgfId-1081630]##This example illustrates how to bind a XML
schema type to a Java type different from the default one.

[#50536467_pgfId-1081631]##XML Schema fragment:

[#50536467_pgfId-1081632]##<xs:element name="partNumber" type="xs:int"/>

[#50536467_pgfId-1081633]##Customization:

[#50536467_pgfId-1081634]##<jaxb:globalBindings>

[#50536467_pgfId-1081635]## ....

[#50536467_pgfId-1081636]## <jaxb:javaType name="long"

[#50536467_pgfId-1081637]## xmlType="xs:int"/>

[#50536467_pgfId-1081638]##</jaxb:globalBindings>

[#50536467_pgfId-1081639]##Since a Java built-in is specified, a parse
or a print method need not be specified. A JAXB implementation uses the
parse and print methods defined in _DatatypeConverter_ class for
converting between lexical representations and values. A JAXB
implementation unmarshals an input value using the following methods:

[#50536467_pgfId-1081640]## int j =
(int)DataTypeConverter.parseLong(string);

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1081627]##Events

[#50536467_pgfId-1078671]##The parse method _parseMethod_ may fail,
since it is only defined on those strings that are valid representations
of target Java datatype values and it can be applied to arbitrary
strings. A parse method must indicate failure by throwing an exception
of whatever type is appropriate, though it should never throw a
_TypeConstraintException_ . A JAXB unmarshaller process must ensure that
an exception thrown by a parse method is caught and, if appropriate, a
_parseConversionEvent_ event is generated.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078672]##The print method _printMethod_ usually does
not fail. If it does, then the JAXB implementation must ensure that the
exception thrown by a print method is caught and a
_printConversionEvent_ is generated.

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078673]##Customization Overrides

[#50536467_pgfId-1078674]##The _<javaType>_ overrides the default
binding of _xmlType_ to the Java datatype specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536464_60588[See Java Mapping for XML Schema Built-in
Types].

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078679]##[#50536467_68898]##Customizable Schema Elements

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1078680]##Simple Type Definition

[#50536467_pgfId-1078681]##A _<javaType>_ binding declaration is allowed
in the annotation element of the of a simple type definition. The
_javaType_ overrides the default binding of _xmlType_ to the Java
datatype specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536464_60588[See Java Mapping for
XML Schema Built-in Types]. The customization values defined have
definition scope and thus covers all references to this simple type
definition.

[#50536467_pgfId-1097605]##If the simple type definition is mapped to a
schema-derived type, an _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ is generated on that
class. Annotation element _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter.value()_ is set to a
generated classlink:#pgfId-1097667[28] that extends
_javax.xml.bind.annotation.adapter.XmlAdapter_ . The generated class’
_unmarshal_ method must call the <javaType> customization’s parse
method, which is specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_72052[See
<javaType> Declaration]. The generated class’ _marshal_ method must call
the <javaType> customization’s print method.

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1083379]## _GlobalBindings_

[#50536467_pgfId-1083380]##A _<javaType>_ binding declaration is allowed
as part of _<globalBindings>._ The _javaType_ overrides the default
binding of _xmlType_ to the Java datatype specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536464_60588[See Java Mapping for XML Schema Built-in
Types]. The customization values defined have global scope.

[#50536467_pgfId-1097659]##For each element or attribute declaration
that references an _xmlType_ that has a globalBindings _<javaType>_
customization specified for it, the corresponding JAXB property is
annotated with _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ .

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1097660]## _<property><baseType>_ declaration

[#50536467_pgfId-1092646]##A _<javaType>_ binding declaration is allowed
as part of _<baseType>_ in the _<property>_ binding declaration. The
_javaType_ overrides the default binding of _xmlType_ to the Java
datatype specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536464_60588[See Java Mapping for
XML Schema Built-in Types]. Additional semantics are specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_98204[See baseType]” also
apply.[#50536467_25293]##

[#50536467_pgfId-1097612]##The schema-derived JAXB property is annotated
with _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_98204[See baseType]”.

== [#50536467_pgfId-1092655]##[#50536467_93416]## _<typesafeEnum>_ Declaration

[#50536467_pgfId-1092656]##This binding declaration allows the
customization of a binding of an XML schema element to its Java
representation as an enum type, Section 8.9 in [JLS3]. Only simple type
definitions with enumeration facets can be customized using this binding
declaration.

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078731]##[#50536467_17922]##Usage

[#50536467_pgfId-1078732]##<typesafeEnumClass> +
[ name = "enumClassName" ] +
[ map = “true” | “false” | “1” | “0” ] +
[ ref = "enumClassName" ] +
[ <typesafeEnumMember> ... </typesafeEnumMember> ]* +
[ <javadoc> enumClassJavadoc </javadoc> ] +
</typesafeEnumClass> +
 +
<typesafeEnumMember name = "enumMemberName"> +
[ value = "enumMemberValue"] +
[ <javadoc> enumMemberJavadoc </javadoc> ] +
</typesafeEnumMember>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078741]##There are two binding declarations
_<typesafeEnumClass>_ and _<typesafeEnumMember>_ . The two binding
declarations allow the enumeration members of an enumeration class and
enumeration class itself to be customized independently.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078742]##The < _typesafeEnumClass>_ declaration
defines the following customization values:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1083846]## _name_ defines the customization value
_enumClassName_ , if specified. _enumClassName_ must be a legal Java
Identifier; it must not have a package prefix. +
 +
For an anonymous simple type, the _name_ attribute must be present. If
absent, it must result in an invalid customization as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid Customizations].”
* [#50536467_pgfId-1096700]## _map_ determines if the simple type
definition should be bound to an enum type. When _map_ ’s value is
_false_ , then the simple type definition must not be bound to an enum
type. _map_ defaults to _true_ .
* [#50536467_pgfId-1100271]## _ref_ if specified, is the name of the
enum class that is provided outside the schema compiler. This
customization causes a schema compiler to refer to this external enum,
as opposed to generate a definition. It must include the complete
package name. This attribute is mutually exclusive with the _className_
attribute and the _map_ attribute.
* [#50536467_pgfId-1083848]## _<javadoc>_ element, if specified
customizes the Javadoc for the enumeration class. _<_ _javadoc>_ defines
the customization value _enumClassjavadoc_ if specified as described in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_64915[See <javadoc> Declaration].”
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078748]##Zero or more _<typesafeEnumMember>_
declarations. The customization values are as defined as specified by
the _<typesafeEnumMember>_ declaration.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078749]##The _<typesafeEnumMember>_ declaration
defines the following customization values:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1083835]## _name_ must always be specified and
defines a customization value _enumMemberName_ . _enumMemberName_ must
be a legal Java identifier.
* [#50536467_pgfId-1083837]## _value_ defines a customization value
_enumMemberValue_ , if specified. _enumMemberValue_ must be the
enumeration value specified in the source schema. The usage of _value_
is further constrained as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_50888[See
value Attribute].”
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078755]## _<javadoc>_ if specified, customizes the
Javadoc for the enumeration constant. _<javadoc>_ defines a
customization value _enumMemberjavadoc_ if specified as described in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_64915[See <javadoc> Declaration].”

[#50536467_pgfId-1084620]##For inline annotation, the
_<typesafeEnumClass>_ must be specified in the annotation element of the
< _simpleType_ > element. The _<typesafeEnumMember>_ must be specified
in the annotation element of the enumeration member. This allows the
enumeration member to be customized independently from the enumeration
class.

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078761]## _value_ [#50536467_50888]## Attribute

[#50536467_pgfId-1078762]##The purpose of the _value_ attribute is to
support customization of an enumeration value using an external binding
syntax. When the _<typesafeEnumMember>_ is used in an inline annotation,
the enumeration value being customized can be identified by the
annotation element with which it is associated. However, when an
external binding declaration is used, while possible, it is not
desirable to use XPath to identify an enumeration value.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078763]##So when customizing using external binding
syntax, the _value_ attribute must be provided. This serves as a key to
identify the enumeration value to which the _<typesafeEnumMember>_
applies. It’s use is therefore further constrained as follows:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1078764]##When _<typesafeEnumMember>_ is specified in
the annotation element of the enumeration member or when XPath refers
directly to a single enumeration facet, then the value attribute must be
absent. If present, it must result in must result in an invalid
customization as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid
Customizations].”
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078765]##When _<typesafeEnumMember>_ is scoped to
the _typesafeEnumClass_ declaration, the value attribute must be
present. If absent, it must result in must result in an invalid
customization as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid
Customizations].” The enumMemberValue must be used to identify the
enumeration member to which the _<typesafeEnumMember>_ applies.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078768]##An example of external binding syntax can be
found in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_96136[See Example 2: typesafeEnum
Customization: External Binding Declaration].”

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078770]##Inline Annotations

[#50536467_pgfId-1078771]##There are two ways to customize an
enumeration class:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1078772]##split inline annotation
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078773]##combined inline annotation

[#50536467_pgfId-1078774]##In split inline annotation, the enumeration
value and the enumeration class are customized separately i.e. the
_<typesafeEnumMember>_ is used independently not as a child element of
_<typesafeEnumClass>._ An example of this is shown in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_64175[See Example 1: typesafeEnum Customization:
Split Inline Annotation].”

[#50536467_pgfId-1078778]##In combined inline annotation, the
enumeration value and the enumeration class are customized together i.e.
the _<typesafeEnumMember>_ is used as a child element of
_<typesafeEnumClass>._ This is similar to the customization used in
external binding declaration. In this case the _value_ attribute must be
present in the _<typesafeEnumMember>_ for reasons noted in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_50888[See value Attribute].” An example of this
customization is shown in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_12334[See Example 3:
typesafeEnum Customization: Combined Inline Annotation].”

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078785]##Customization Overrides

[#50536467_pgfId-1078786]##When binding a schema type definition’s Java
representation to an enum type, the following customization values
override the defaults specified in Chapter 5. It is specified in a
common section here and referenced from link:jaxb.htm#50536467_68077[See
Customizable Schema Elements].”

* [#50536467_pgfId-1078790]##name: If enumClassName is defined, then the
name obtained by mapping enumClassName as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_37846[See Customized Name Mapping].”
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078794]##package name: The name obtained by
inheriting _packgeName_ from a scope that covers this schema element and
mapping packageName as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_37846[See
Customized Name Mapping].”
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078798]##enumclass javadoc: _enumClassJavaDoc_ if
defined, customizes the _class/interface section (_
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_94945[See Javadoc Sections]”) for the enumeration
class, as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_50461[See Javadoc
Customization].”
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078805]##enum constant set: Each member of the set
is computed as follows:
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078806]## name: If enumMemberName is defined, the
name obtained by mapping enumMemberName as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_37846[See Customized Name Mapping].”
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078810]##javadoc: _enumMemberJavaDoc_ if defined,
customizes the _field section (_ link:jaxb.htm#50536467_94945[See
Javadoc Sections]” ) for the enumeration class, as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_50461[See Javadoc Customization].”

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078822]##[#50536467_15839]##Customizable Schema Elements

[#50536467_pgfId-1078823]##Any XML Schema simple type which has an
enumeration facet can be customized with _<jaxb:typesafeEnumClass>_
declaration with the following exception. If the simple type definition
derives from _xs:QName. xs:NOTATIION, xs:base64Binary, xs:hexBinary,
xs:date, xs:time, xs:dateTime, xs:duration, xs:gDay, xs:gMonth,
xs:gYear, xs:gMonthDay, xs:gYearMonth, xs:IDREF, xs:ID_ , it must result
in an invalid customization as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid Customizations].”. Since most
of these Xml datatypes bind to a mutable Java type, instances of these
Java types are not sufficient to be an immutable value of an enum
constant.

* [#50536467_pgfId-1098108]##

====== [#50536467_pgfId-1078825]##[#50536467_64175]##Example 1: typesafeEnum Customization: Split Inline Annotation

[#50536467_pgfId-1078826]##XML Schema fragment:

[#50536467_pgfId-1078827]##<xs:simpleType name="USState"> +
<xs:annotation><xs:appinfo> +
<jaxb:typesafeEnumClass name="USStateAbbr"/> +
</xs:appinfo></xs:annotation> +
<xs:restriction base="xs:NCName"> +
<xs:enumeration value="AK"> +
<xs:annotation><xs:appinfo> +
<jaxb:typesafeEnumMember name="STATE_AK"/> +
</xs:appinfo></xs:annotation> +
</xs:enumeration> +
<xs:enumeration value="AL"> +
<xs:annotation><xs:appinfo> +
<jaxb:typesafeEnumMember name="STATE_AL"/> +
</xs:appinfo></xs:annotation> +
</xs:enumeration> +
</xs:restriction> +
</xs:simpleType>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078844]##Customized derived code:

[#50536467_pgfId-1078845]##public enum USStateAbbr \{ +
STATE_AL, STATE_AK; +
public String value() \{ return name(); } +
public static USStateAbbr fromValue(String value) \{ ... } +
};

====== [#50536467_pgfId-1078863]##[#50536467_96136]##Example 2: typesafeEnum Customization: External Binding Declaration

[#50536467_pgfId-1078864]##The following example shows how to customize
the above XML schema fragment using an external binding syntax.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078865]##<jaxb:typesafeEnumClass name="USStateAbbr"> +
<jaxb:typesafeEnumMember name="STATE_AK" value="AK"> +
<jaxb:typesafeEnumMember name="STATE_AL" value="AL"/> +
</jaxb:typesafeEnumClass>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078869]##The attribute _value_ must be specified for
_<typesafeEnumMember>_ . This identifies the enumeration member to which
_<typesafeEnumMember>_ applies.

====== [#50536467_pgfId-1078871]##[#50536467_12334]##Example 3: typesafeEnum Customization: Combined Inline Annotation

[#50536467_pgfId-1078872]##The following example shows how to customize
the above XML schema fragment using inline annotation which does not
split the external binding syntax.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078873]##<xs:simpleType name="USState"> +
<xs:annotation><xs:appinfo> +
<jaxb:typesafeEnumClass name="USStateAbbr"> +
<jaxb:typesafeEnumMember name="STATE_AK" value="AK"/> +
<jaxb:typesafeEnumMember name="STATE_AL" value="AL"/> +
</jaxb:typesafeEnumClass> +
</xs:appinfo></xs:annotation> +
<xs:restriction base="xs:NCName"> +
<xs:enumeration value="AK"/> +
<xs:enumeration value="AL"/> +
</xs:restriction> +
</xs:simpleType>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078884]##The attribute value must be specified for
_typesafeEnumMember_ . This identifies the enumeration member to which
the binding declaration applies.

== [#50536467_pgfId-1078886]## _<javadoc>_ [#50536467_64915]## Declaration

[#50536467_pgfId-1078887]##The _<javadoc>_ declaration allows the
customization of a javadoc that is generated when an XML schema
component is bound to its Java representation.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078888]##This binding declaration is not a global XML
element. Hence it can only be used as a local element within the content
model of another binding declaration. The binding declaration in which
it is used determines the section of the Javadoc that is customized.

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078890]##[#50536467_94945]##Javadoc Sections

[#50536467_pgfId-1078891]##The terminology used for the javadoc sections
is derived from “Requirements for Writing Java API Specifications” which
can be found online at http:
_//java.sun.com/j2se/javadoc/writingapispecs/index.html._

[#50536467_pgfId-1078892]##The following sections are defined for the
purposes for customization:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1078893]##package section (corresponds to package
specification)
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078894]##class/interface section (corresponds to
class/interface specification)
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078895]##method section (corresponds to method
specification)
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078896]##field section (corresponds to field
specification)

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1078897]##Usage

[#50536467_pgfId-1078898]##Note that the text content of a _<javadoc>_
element must use _CDATA_ or _&lt;_ to escape embedded HTML tags.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078899]##<javadoc>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078900]## Contents in &lt;b>Javadoc&lt;\b> format.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078901]##</javadoc>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078902]##or

[#50536467_pgfId-1078903]##<javadoc>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078904]## <<![CDATA[

[#50536467_pgfId-1078905]## Contents in <b>Javadoc<\b> format

[#50536467_pgfId-1078906]## ]]>

[#50536467_pgfId-1078907]##</javadoc>

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1083872]##[#50536467_50461]##Javadoc Customization

[#50536467_pgfId-1083873]##The Javadoc must be generated from the
_<javadoc>_ element if specified. The Javadoc section depends upon where
_<javadoc>_ element is used. JAXB providers may generate additional
provider specific Javadoc information (for example, contents of the
_<xs:documentation>_ element).

== [#50536467_pgfId-1078912]## _<dom>_ [#50536467_10640]## Declaration

[#50536467_pgfId-1094124]##The _<dom>_ customization binds an XML Schema
component to DOM rather than to a strongly typed Java representation.
Specifically, JAXB bindings for mixed content and wildcard result in a
hybrid mixture of strongly typed Java instances with DOM nodes or
java.lang.String, representing text info. These mixed bindings might be
more easily processed solely as one form, namely as an XML fragment
represented as DOM. This customization also meets a JAX-WS 2.0
databinding requirement from link:jaxb.htm#50536483_56011[See Disabling
Databinding]”.

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1094528]##Usage

[#50536467_pgfId-1094560]##The syntax for the customization is the
following:

[#50536467_pgfId-1094565]##<dom [ [type= "w3c" |
_otherDomRepresentations_ ] />

[#50536467_pgfId-1094566]##You can use the optional type attribute to
specify the type of DOM. By default, it is W3C DOM.

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1099101]##[#50536467_74505]##Customizable Schema Elements

[#50536467_pgfId-1099104]##This customization can be attached to the
following XML Schema components:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1094531]##Element declaration ( _<xs:element>_ )
* [#50536467_pgfId-1094532]##Type definition ( _<xs:complexType>_ and
_<xs:simpleType>_ )
* [#50536467_pgfId-1094533]##Wildcard ( _<xs:any>_ )
* [#50536467_pgfId-1094534]##Model groups ( _<xs:choice>_ _,_ _<xs:all>_
_,_ _<xs:sequence>_ )
* [#50536467_pgfId-1094535]##Model group definition ( _<xs:group>_ )
* [#50536467_pgfId-1094536]##Particle

[#50536467_pgfId-1099218]##For all of the above cases, the Java
representation of the DOM element is an instance of the Element class
for the specified DOM representation. For example, W3C DOM element is
bound to _org.w3c.dom.Element_ .

[#50536467_pgfId-1099097]##Special Case Handling of DOM customization on
a:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1099149]## _type definition_ - it is semantically
equivalent to placing the dom customization on each element declaration
referencing that type definition.
* [#50536467_pgfId-1099158]## _global element declaration_ - it is
semantically equivalent to placing the dom customization on each element
declaration referencing, via _@ref_ , the global element declaration.
The dom customization on the global element declaration does not cause
that element to be unmarshalled as DOM when it is the root element of an
XML document nor when the element is part of a wildcard content JAXB
property.
* [#50536467_pgfId-1099159]## _mixed content_ - if an XML schema
component is annotated with a _dom_ customization and that XML schema
component can contain character data information due to its parent
complex type definition being defined with mixed content, character data
information is handled as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536464_49145[See
Bind mixed content]”.

[#50536467_pgfId-1099235]##The dom customization allows one to disable
databinding and process a part of a document using other technologies
that require “raw” XML.

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1094482]##Examples

====== [#50536467_pgfId-1094466]##Wildcard Binding Example

[#50536467_pgfId-1099224]##A wildcard is mapped to a List of
_org.w3c.dom.Element_ . Each element that matches to the wildcard will
be turned into a DOM tree.

[#50536467_pgfId-1094467]##<xs:complexType name=”foo”> +
<xs:sequence> +
<xs:any maxOccurs="unbounded" processContents="lax"> +
_<xs:annotation><xs:appinfo> +
<jaxb:dom/> +
</xs:appinfo></xs:annotation> +
_ </xs:any> +
</xs:sequence> +
</xs:complexType>

[#50536467_pgfId-1094463]## +
import org.w3c.dom.Element; +
public class Foo \{ +
@XmlAnyElement(lax=”false”) +
List<Element> getContent()\{...} +
}

====== [#50536467_pgfId-1099178]##Wildcard and Mixed Content Binding Example

[#50536467_pgfId-1099182]##If the complexType definition above is
defined to have mixed content, due to element _[complexType]_ __ having
attribute _@mixed=”true”_ , the JAXB binding is:

[#50536467_pgfId-1099191]##import org.w3c.dom.Element; +
public class Foo \{ +
/* Element content is represented _org.w3c.dom.Element_ . +
* Character data information is represented as instances of +
* _java.lang.String_ . */ +
@XmlMixed +
@XmlAnyElement(lax=”false”) +
List<Object> getContent()\{...} +
}

== [#50536467_pgfId-1097714]## _<inlineBinaryData>_ [#50536467_69189]## Declaration

[#50536467_pgfId-1097929]##The _<inlineBinaryData>_ customization
provides declarative control over the optimization for binary data
described in link:jaxb.htm#50536486_13271[See Appendix],
link:jaxb.htm#50536486_24738[See Enhanced Binary Data Handling].

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1097936]##Usage

[#50536467_pgfId-1097720]##The syntax for the customization is the
following:

[#50536467_pgfId-1097721]##<inlineBinaryData/>

[#50536467_pgfId-1097723]##This customization disables considering the
binary data optimization for a schema component containing binary data.

[#50536467_pgfId-1097781]##This customization can be attached to the
following XML Schema components:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1097724]##Element declaration ( _<xs:element>_ ) with
binary data or
* [#50536467_pgfId-1097725]##Type definition ( _<xs:complexType>_ and
_<xs:simpleType>_ ) deriving from binary datatype

[#50536467_pgfId-1097944]##When a schema component that binds to a JAXB
property is customized with <inlineBinaryData>, its schema-derived JAXB
property is annotated with _@XmlInlineBinaryData_ . When a type
definition is customized with <inlineBinaryData>, its schema-derived
class is annotated with program annotation _@XmlInlineBinaryData_ .

== [#50536467_pgfId-1098415]## _<factoryMethod>_ Declaration

[#50536467_pgfId-1098438]##The _<factoryMethod>_ customization provides
declarative control over an element or type factory method name
generated in a package’s _ObjectFactory_ class introduced in
link:jaxb.htm#50536473_80810[See Java Package].”. This customization is
useful to resolve name collisions between factory methods in the
schema-derived _ObjectFactory_ class.

==== [#50536467_pgfId-1098450]##Usage

[#50536467_pgfId-1098455]##The syntax for the customization is the
following:

[#50536467_pgfId-1098456]##<factoryMethod
name=”BaseForFactoryMethodName”/>

[#50536467_pgfId-1098466]##The customization value defined is:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1098467]## _name -_ each character of name must be a
valid part of a Java identifier as determined by
_java.lang.Character.isJavaIdentifierPart()._

[#50536467_pgfId-1098481]##The name of the factory method is generated
by concatenating the following components:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1098485]##The string constant _create_
* [#50536467_pgfId-1098486]## _@name_ ’s value

===== [#50536467_pgfId-1098554]##Usage Constraints

[#50536467_pgfId-1098555]##The usage constraints on _<factoryMethod>_
are specified below. Any constraint violation must result in an invalid
customization as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536467_20413[See Invalid
Customizations].” The usage constraints are:

. [#50536467_pgfId-1098559]## _<factoryMethod>_ is only allowed to
annotate an element declaration or a type definition.

[#50536467_pgfId-1098920]##Note that this customization does not require
a factory method to be generated, it simply provides a factory method
name if a factory method is to be generated for the annotated element
declaration or type definition. Section 6 and 7 specifies when a factory
method is generated for an element declarations or type definitions.

== [#50536467_pgfId-1096057]##[#50536467_30958]##Annotation Restrictions

[#50536467_pgfId-1078913]##[XSD PART 1] allows an annotation element to
be specified for most elements but is ambiguous in some cases. The
ambiguity and the way they are addressed are described here.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078914]##The source of ambiguity is related to the
specification of an annotation element for a reference to a schema
element using the “ref” attribute. This arises in three cases:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1078915]##A local attribute references a global
attribute declaration using the “ref” attribute.
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078916]##A local element in a particle references a
global element declaration using the “ref” attribute.
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078917]##A model group in a particle references a
model group definition using the “ref” attribute.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078918]##For example in the following schema fragment
(for brevity, the declaration of the global element “Name” and “Address”
has been omitted).

[#50536467_pgfId-1078919]## _<xs:element name = "Customer">_

[#50536467_pgfId-1078920]## _<xs:complexType>_

[#50536467_pgfId-1078921]## _<xs:element ref = "Name"/>_

[#50536467_pgfId-1078922]## _<xs:element ref = "Address" />_

[#50536467_pgfId-1078923]## _</xs:complexType>_

[#50536467_pgfId-1078924]## _</xs:element>_

[#50536467_pgfId-1078925]##XML Schema spec is ambiguous on whether an
annotation element can be specified at the reference to the “Name”
element.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078926]##The restrictions on annotation elements has
been submitted as an issue to the W3C Schema Working Group along with
JAXB technology requirements (which is that annotations should be
allowed anywhere). Pending a resolution, the semantics of annotation
elements where the XML spec is unclear are assumed as specified as
follows.

[#50536467_pgfId-1078927]##This specification assumes that an annotation
element can be specified in each of the three cases outlined above.
Furthermore, an annotation element is assumed to be associated with the
abstract schema component as follows:

* [#50536467_pgfId-1078928]##The annotation element on an attribute ref
is associated with \{Attribute Use}
* [#50536467_pgfId-1078929]##The annotation element on a model group ref
or an element reference is associated with the \{particle}.

=== [#50536452_pgfId-905380]##Chapter

[#50536452_pgfId-905381]##[#50536452_74620]##Java Types To XML

== [#50536452_pgfId-905382]##Introduction

[#50536452_pgfId-914296]##This chapter specifies the mapping from
program elements to XML Schema. The mapping includes a default as well
as a customized mapping.

== [#50536452_pgfId-885004]##Overview

[#50536452_pgfId-903680]##This section is non normative and provides a
high level view of Java to XML Schema mapping targeted towards both JAXB
application developers and JAXB implementation vendors.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-905348]##Mapping Scope

[#50536452_pgfId-906040]##The mapping covers program elements commonly
used in the composition of a data model for an application: package,
field, property and types (classes and enum construct). Additionally,
the mapping scope also covers mapping annotations used to annotate
schema derived code.

[#50536452_pgfId-906043]##In so far as possible, a program element is
mapped to an equivalent XML Schema construct in an intuitive manner.
Thus,

* [#50536452_pgfId-891420]##Package maps to a XML target namespace. A
package provides a naming context for types. A XML target namespace
provides a naming context for schema components such as elements, type
definitions.
* [#50536452_pgfId-891519]##Type maps to a schema type. A value type is
a data container for values; e.g. a value class contains values
represented by it’s properties and fields. A schema type is a datatype,
an instance of which (e.g. element) acts as a data container for values
represented by schema components within a schema type’s content model
(e.g. element, attributes, etc.). Thus a type maps naturally to a schema
type. For e.g.,
* [#50536452_pgfId-903715]## class typically maps to a complex type
definition
* [#50536452_pgfId-903722]##java primitive types and wrapper classes map
to XML Schema simple type definition.
* [#50536452_pgfId-903691]##Field or property maps to an element or an
attribute contained within the complex type to which a type is mapped.
* [#50536452_pgfId-906038]##Enum type maps to a simple schema type
constrained by enumeration facets.

[#50536452_pgfId-903693]##The input to the mapping process is one or
more sets of packages or classes. A package or a class is mapped and
recursively, fields, properties and types contained with it. The mapping
is customizable.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-905357]##Mapping Annotations

[#50536452_pgfId-891355]##Mapping annotationsThe mapping of program
elements to XML Schema construct can be customized using mapping
annotations, program annotations based on JSR 175 program annotation
facility. Mapping annotations are used for:

* [#50536452_pgfId-906076]##customizing the Java to XML schema mapping.
* [#50536452_pgfId-906080]##annotating schema derived code.
* [#50536452_pgfId-926104]##control over optimized binary data encoding.

[#50536452_pgfId-900036]##The mapping annotations are described in the
_javax.xml.bind.annotation_ and _javax.xml.bind.annotation.adapters_
packages.

[#50536452_pgfId-900137]##Retention Policy The retention policy of all
mapping annotations is RetentionPolicy.RUNTIME. This policy allows
introspection of mapping annotations at runtime. Introspection can be
used by JAXB binding framework to marshal/unmarshal an object graph to
XML representation or to customize the mapping of program elements to
XML Schema constructs. This policy also allows a JAXB vendor
implementation to generate a schema from a program element’s compiled
form rather than its source.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-905385]##XML Name Derivation

[#50536452_pgfId-933218]##Mapped program element is a program element
that has been mapped to an XML Schema construct. It is possible to use
_@XmlTransient_ annotation type to prevent the mapping of a program
element.

[#50536452_pgfId-914286]##XML Names An XML name may be needed for the
schema components for a mapped program element, for e.g. element name.
XML names are usually derived from a program element name, for e.g.
property, field, class name etc.But they can be customized using mapping
annotation. When an XML name is derived from a property name, bean de
capitalization rules are used. If a Java Identifier is not a legal XML
name, then a legal XML name can be assigned using an annotation element
(e.g. _@XmlType(name=”foo”)_ ).

==== [#50536452_pgfId-914287]##Fields and Properties

[#50536452_pgfId-915524]##XML global element Fields and properties
typically map to local elements within a complex type for a class. But a
well formed XML document begins with a root element (a global element in
the corresponding schema). The _@XmlRootElement_ annotation can be used
to associate a global element with a class or an enum type.

[#50536452_pgfId-926294]##Null Value and Nillable Element A null value
for a type mapped to an XML Schema element in two ways: absence of an
element or an nillable element. The mapping annotation for an element
allows either mapping.

[#50536452_pgfId-926295]## 

==== [#50536452_pgfId-926296]##Type Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-926856]##Legacy applications One of the primary use
cases for Java language to XML Schema mapping is to allow an existing
application to be exported as a web service. In many cases, the existing
applications are legacy applications consisting of classes that follow
different class designs. The annotations and default mapping are
designed to enable such classes to be mapped to schema with minimal
changes to existing code. See link:jaxb.htm#50536452_90141[See Default
Mapping] for default mapping.

[#50536452_pgfId-926947]##Class A class usually maps to a complex type.
However, using _@XmlValue_ annotation, a class can also be mapped to a
simple type (to hold a simple value) or a complexType with simpleContent
(to hold a simple value and attributes). The _@XmlType_ annotation can
be used to customize the mapping of a class. For example, it can be used
to map a class to an anonymous type or to control the ordering of
properties and/or fields. Properties and fields are unordered; but they
can be mapped to a content model that is ordered (e.g. xs:sequence) or
unordered content model (xs:all).

[#50536452_pgfId-926877]##Class Designs A class with a public or
protected no-arg constructor can be mapped. If a class has a static
zero-arg factory method, then the factory method can be specified using
the annotation element _@XmlType.factoryMethod()_ and
_@XmlType.factoryClass()_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-926878]##Ordering of Properties/fields: The ordering of
properties and fields can be customized in one of two ways: at the
package level using @XmlAccessorOrder or using _@XmlType.propOrder()_ at
the class level.

[#50536452_pgfId-905164]##Class Hierarchy Mapping Class hierarchy
typically maps to a type derivation hierarchy. The _@XmlType_ and
_@XmlValue_ annotations together provide support mapping class hierarchy
to schema type hierarchy where XML Schema complex type derives by
extension from either another complex type or a simple type.

[#50536452_pgfId-915531]##Supported Collection Types Typed collections
and untyped collections are mapped. Mapped collection types are: arrays,
indexed properties and parametric types. Mapped untyped collection are:
_java.util.List_ , _java.util.Set_ and _java.util.HashMap_ . Of these,
_java.util.HashMap_ does not map naturally to a XML Schema construct.
For example, _HashMap_ can have different XML serialized forms which
differ in trade-offs made between memory and speed or specificity and
generality. The XML serialization form can be customized using
_@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ (link:jaxb.htm#50536452_29781[See Adapter]”).

[#50536452_pgfId-904482]##Collection serialized forms A collection type
can be mapped to a XML Schema complex type and collection item is mapped
to local element within it. Alternately, a parameterized collection
(e.g. List<Integer>) can be mapped to a simple schema type that derives
by list.

[#50536452_pgfId-926832]##When a collection type is mapped to a XML
Schema complex type, the mapping is designed to support two forms of
serialization shown below.

[#50536452_pgfId-904721]##//Example: code fragment +
int[] names; +
 +
// XML Serialization Form 1 (Unwrapped collection) +
// Element name is derived from property or field name +
<names> ... </names> +
<names> ... </names> +
... +
 +
// XML Serialization Form 2 ( Wrapped collection ) +
// Element name of wrapper is derived from property or field name +
// Element name of each item in collection is also derived from

[#50536452_pgfId-914228]##// property name +
<names> +
<names> value-of-item </names> +
<names> value-of-item </names> +
.... +
</names>

[#50536452_pgfId-904720]##The two serialized XML forms allow a null
collection to be represented either by absence or presence of an element
with a nillable attribute. The _@XmlElementWrapper_ annotation on the
property or field is used to customize the schema corresponding to the
above XML serialization forms.

[#50536452_pgfId-925369]##A parameterized collection (e.g.
List<Integer>) can also be mapped to simple schema that derives by list
using _@XmlList_ annotation. For e.g. the serialized XML form is: “1 2 3
“.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-905361]##[#50536452_29781]##Adapter

[#50536452_pgfId-897563]##A type may not map naturally to a XML
representation (see Supported Collection Types above). As another
example, a single instance of a type may have different on wire XML
serialization forms.

[#50536452_pgfId-905556]##Adapter approach defines a portable
customization mechanism for applications exemplified above. The
mechanism provides a way to adapt a bound type, a Java type used to
process XML content, to value type, mapped to an XML representation or
vice versa. It is the value type that is used for marshalling and
unmarshalling. Use of this approach involves two steps:

* [#50536452_pgfId-912052]##provide an adapter class that extends the
abstract class _@javax.xml.bind.annotation.adapters.XmlAdapter_ that
defines two methods _unmarshal()_ and _marshal()_ . The methods are
invoked by JAXB vendor implementation during unmarshalling and
marshaling respectively to adapt between bound and value types.
* [#50536452_pgfId-929345]##specify the adapter class using the
_@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ annotation.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-929346]##Referential Integrity

[#50536452_pgfId-899465]##Preserving referential integrity of an object
graph across XML serialization followed by a XML de serialization,
requires an object reference to be marshalled by reference or
containment appropriately. Possible strategies include:

* [#50536452_pgfId-899597]##marshal all references to a given object by
reference.
* [#50536452_pgfId-899602]##marshal the first reference to an object by
containment and subsequent references to the same object by reference.

[#50536452_pgfId-899604]##Depending on the strategy, the schema to which
program element is mapped also varies accordingly.

[#50536452_pgfId-904000]##Two annotations _@XmlID_ and _@XmlIDREF_
provide the mechanism which can be used together to map program element
by reference or containment. This places the burden of preserving
referential integrity on a developer. On the other hand, the ability to
customize the mapping is useful since it can result in mapping of
program elements to a schema that defines a document structure more
meaningfully to an application than a default derived schema.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-905373]##Property/Field Name Collision

[#50536452_pgfId-903473]##A XML name collision can arise when the
property name obtained by bean de capitalization and the name of a field
map to a same schema component. For example

[#50536452_pgfId-904913]##public int item;

[#50536452_pgfId-903482]##pubilc int getItem();

[#50536452_pgfId-903483]##public void setItem(int val);

[#50536452_pgfId-915579]##The name collision occurs because the property
name, bean de capitalization, and the name of the public field are both
the same i.e. _item._ In the case, where the property and the public
field refer to the same field, the _@XmlTransient_ can be used to
resolve the name collision by preventing the mapping of either the
public field or the property.

== [#50536452_pgfId-915580]##Naming Conventions

[#50536452_pgfId-886524]##Any source and schema fragments and examples
shown in this chapter are meant to be illustrative rather than
normative.

* [#50536452_pgfId-885433]## _@XmlAttribute_ denotes both a program
annotation type as well a specific use of annotation type.
* [#50536452_pgfId-885437]##The prefix _xs:_ is used to refer to schema
components in W3C XML Schema namespace.[#50536452_20413]##
* [#50536452_pgfId-925051]##The prefix _ref:_ is used to refer to schema
components in the namespace _“http://ws-i.org/profiles/basic/1.1/xsd”_
* [#50536452_pgfId-905681]##

== [#50536452_pgfId-900121]##Constraint Violations

[#50536452_pgfId-905621]##For the purpose of mapping and constraint
checking, if a program element is not annotated explicitly, and there is
a default mapping annotation defined for that element, it must be
applied first before performing any constraint checks or mapping. This
is assumed in the normative mapping tables shown below.

[#50536452_pgfId-931165]##The mapping of program elements to XML Schema
constructs is subject to mapping constraints, specified elsewhere in
this chapter. The mapping constraints must be enforced by the
_javax.xml.bind.annotation.JAXBContext.newInstance(..)_ method. Any
cycles resulting from a combination of annotations or default mapping
must be detected in
_javax.xml.bind.annotation.JAXBContext.newInstance(..)_ method and also
constitutes a constraint violation. A _javax.xml.bind.JAXBException_ or
(its subclass, which can be provider specific) must be thrown upon a
constraint violation.

[#50536452_pgfId-925350]##A JAXB Provider must support the schema
generation at runtime. See
_javax.xml.bind.JAXBContext.generateSchema(..)_ for more information.

== [#50536452_pgfId-900125]##[#50536452_89210]##Type Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-900122]##This section specifies the mapping of Java
types to XML Schema.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-885386]##Java Primitive types

[#50536452_pgfId-905419]##The default mapping of Java types (and their
wrapper classes) specified in table link:jaxb.htm#50536452_19839[See
Mapping: Java Primitive types to Schema Types] must be supported.

======= [#50536452_pgfId-905424]##[#50536452_19839]##Mapping: Java Primitive types to Schema Types

[#50536452_pgfId-905428]##Java Primitive Type

[#50536452_pgfId-905430]##XML data type

[#50536452_pgfId-905432]##boolean

[#50536452_pgfId-905434]##xs:boolean

[#50536452_pgfId-905436]##byte

[#50536452_pgfId-905438]##xs:byte

[#50536452_pgfId-905440]##short

[#50536452_pgfId-905442]##xs:short

[#50536452_pgfId-905444]##int

[#50536452_pgfId-905446]##xs:int

[#50536452_pgfId-905448]##long

[#50536452_pgfId-905450]##xs:long

[#50536452_pgfId-905452]##float

[#50536452_pgfId-905454]##xs:float

[#50536452_pgfId-905456]##double

[#50536452_pgfId-905458]##xs:double

==== [#50536452_pgfId-905510]##Java Standard Classes

[#50536452_pgfId-905463]##The default mapping of Java classes specified
in link:jaxb.htm#50536452_44213[See Mapping of Standard Java classes]
must be supported.

======= [#50536452_pgfId-905466]##[#50536452_44213]##Mapping of Standard Java classes

[#50536452_pgfId-905470]##Java Class

[#50536452_pgfId-905472]##XML data type

[#50536452_pgfId-905474]##java.lang.String

[#50536452_pgfId-905476]##xs:string

[#50536452_pgfId-905478]##java.math.BigInteger

[#50536452_pgfId-905480]##xs:integer

[#50536452_pgfId-905482]##java.math.BigDecimal

[#50536452_pgfId-905484]##xs:decimal

[#50536452_pgfId-905486]##java.util.Calendar

[#50536452_pgfId-905488]##xs:dateTime

[#50536452_pgfId-905490]##java.util.Date

[#50536452_pgfId-905492]##xs:dateTime

[#50536452_pgfId-905494]##javax.xml.namespace.QName

[#50536452_pgfId-905496]##xs:QName

[#50536452_pgfId-905498]##java.net.URI

[#50536452_pgfId-905500]##xs:string

[#50536452_pgfId-905502]##javax.xml.datatype.XMLGregorianCalendar

[#50536452_pgfId-905504]##xs:anySimpleType

[#50536452_pgfId-905506]##javax.xml.datatype.Duration

[#50536452_pgfId-905508]##xs:duration

[#50536452_pgfId-917675]##java.lang.Object

[#50536452_pgfId-921026]##xs:anyType

[#50536452_pgfId-925098]##java.awt.Image

[#50536452_pgfId-925100]##xs:base64Binary

[#50536452_pgfId-925125]##javax.activation.DataHandler

===== [#50536452_pgfId-925525]##Type Variable

[#50536452_pgfId-932224]##The following grammar is from [JLS], Section
4.4, “Type Variables”.

[#50536452_pgfId-932251]## _TypeParameter: +
TypeVariable TypeBoundopt_

[#50536452_pgfId-932403]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-932335]## _TypeBound: +
extends ClassOrInterfaceType AdditionalBoundListopt_

[#50536452_pgfId-925529]##A type variable without a Typebound must be
mapped to xs:anyType.

[#50536452_pgfId-932393]##A type variable with a TypeBound must map to
the schema type to which ClassOrInterfaceType is mapped; the mapping of
ClassOrInterface is subject to the mapping constraints specified in
other sections in this chapter.

[#50536452_pgfId-925535]##<!-- code fragment

[#50536452_pgfId-925549]##public class Shape <T> \{

[#50536452_pgfId-925536]## public T xshape;

[#50536452_pgfId-925537]## public Shape() \{};

[#50536452_pgfId-925538]## public Shape(T f) \{

[#50536452_pgfId-925539]## xshape = f;

[#50536452_pgfId-925540]## }

[#50536452_pgfId-925541]##}

[#50536452_pgfId-925550]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-925551]##<!-- XML Schema

[#50536452_pgfId-925554]##<xs:complexType name="shape">

[#50536452_pgfId-925555]## <xs:sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-925556]## <xs:element name="xshape" type="xs:anyType"
minOccurs="0"/>

[#50536452_pgfId-925708]## </xs:sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-925709]## </xs:complexType>

===== [#50536452_pgfId-925713]##[#50536452_11235]##Type Arguments and Wildcards

[#50536452_pgfId-932413]##The following grammar is from [JLS], Section
4.5.1, “Type Arguments and Wildcards”.

[#50536452_pgfId-932420]##TypeArguments:

[#50536452_pgfId-932450]## <ActualTypeArgumentList>

[#50536452_pgfId-932421]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-932414]##ActualTypeArgumentList:

[#50536452_pgfId-932431]## ActualTypeArgument

[#50536452_pgfId-932429]## ActualTypeArgumentList, ActualTypeArgument

[#50536452_pgfId-932453]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-932435]##ActualTypeArgument:

[#50536452_pgfId-932436]## ReferenceType

[#50536452_pgfId-932454]## Wildcard

[#50536452_pgfId-932457]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-932418]##Wildcard:

[#50536452_pgfId-932458]##?WildcardBounds

[#50536452_pgfId-932415]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-925738]##WildcardBounds:

[#50536452_pgfId-925739]## extends ReferenceType

[#50536452_pgfId-925740]## super ReferenceType

[#50536452_pgfId-925720]##A wildcard without a WildcardBounds must map
to schema type xs:anyType.

[#50536452_pgfId-932474]##A wildcard with a WildcardBounds whose super
type is ReferenceType must map to schema type xs:anyType.

[#50536452_pgfId-925721]##A wildcard with a WildcardBounds that extends
a ReferenceType must map to the schema type to which the ReferenceType
is mapped; this mapping is subject to the mapping constraints specified
in other sections in this chapter and is determined by the annotations
as specified in the mapping tables in the chapter. For example:

[#50536452_pgfId-926005]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-926006]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-925751]##/** EXAMPLE : WildcarType Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-926007]##// Code fragment

[#50536452_pgfId-926010]##public class Shape \{...}

[#50536452_pgfId-925755]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-925756]##public class Rectangle extends Shape \{...}

[#50536452_pgfId-925757]##public class Circle extends Shape \{...}

[#50536452_pgfId-925758]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-925761]##public class Foo \{

[#50536452_pgfId-925762]## public java.util.List<? extends Shape>
shapes;

[#50536452_pgfId-925759]##}

[#50536452_pgfId-925866]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-925867]##<-- XML Schema fragment

[#50536452_pgfId-925908]## ...

[#50536452_pgfId-925909]##</xs:complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-925874]##

[#50536452_pgfId-925876]## <xs:complexContent>

[#50536452_pgfId-925890]## <xs:complexContent>

nillable="true"

==== [#50536452_pgfId-925710]##Collections

[#50536452_pgfId-925685]##The following collection must be supported:

* [#50536452_pgfId-925686]## _java.util.Map_ and its subtypes (e.g.
java.util.HashMap)
* [#50536452_pgfId-925690]## _java.util.Collection_ and it’s subtypes
(e.g. java.util.List)

[#50536452_pgfId-931514]##The mapping of collection depends upon the
annotations on the program elements and is specified in the mapping
tables. This specification uses a collection type to be one of
_java.util.Collection_ (or a subtype derived from it) , an array or an
JavaBean index property.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-911587]##@XmlAccessorType

[#50536452_pgfId-911628]##This annotation allows control over default
serialization of fields and properties.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-911614]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-911594]##@Inherited @Retention(RUNTIME)
@Target(\{PACKAGE, TYPE})

[#50536452_pgfId-911595]##public @interface XmlAccessorType \{

[#50536452_pgfId-911610]## XmlAccessType value() default
XmlAccessType.PUBLIC_MEMBER;

[#50536452_pgfId-911588]##}

[#50536452_pgfId-914409]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-914403]##public enum XmlAccessType \{ NONE, PROPERTY,
FIELD, PUBLIC_MEMBER}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-911805]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-928500]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

[#50536452_pgfId-928501]##This annotation can be used only with the
following other annotations: _@XmlType, @XmlRootElement_ ,
_@XmlAccessorOrder, @XmlSchema, @XmlSchemaType, @XmlSchemaTypes,
@XmlJavaTypeAdapters._ It can also be used with the following
annotations at the package level: _@ XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-911796]##See link:jaxb.htm#50536452_90141[See Default
Mapping]”.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-921103]##[#50536452_66117]##@XmlAccessorOrder

[#50536452_pgfId-927084]##This annotation allows control over the
default ordering of properties and fields that are mapped to XML
elements. Properties and fields mapped to XML attributes are not
impacted by this annotation since XML attributes are unordered.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-921105]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-921106]##@Inhertited @Retention(RUNTIME)
@Target(\{PACKAGE, TYPE})

[#50536452_pgfId-921107]##public @interface XmlAccessorOrder \{

[#50536452_pgfId-921108]## XmlAccessOrder value() default
XmlAccessOrder.UNDEFINED;

[#50536452_pgfId-921109]##}

[#50536452_pgfId-925288]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-925289]##public enum XmlAccessOrder \{ UNDEFINED,
ALPHABETICAL}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-927295]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-928447]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

. [#50536452_pgfId-928474]##[#50536452_37604]##This annotation can be
used only with the following other annotations: _@XmlType,
@XmlRootElement_ , _@XmlAccessorType, @XmlSchema, @XmlSchemaType,
@XmlSchemaTypes, @XmlJavaTypeAdapters._ It can also be used with the
following annotations at the package level: _@ XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-927296]##If the value of _@XmlAccessorOrder.value()_ is
_XmlAccessOrder.ALHPHABETICAL_ , then the default ordering of
fields/properties is lexicographic order as determined by
_java.lang.String.CompareTo((String anotherString)_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-927286]##If the _@XmlAccessorOrder.value()_ is
_XmlAccessOrder.UNDEFINED_ , then the default ordering of
fields/properties is unspecified.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-925160]##[#50536452_35544]##@XmlSchemaType

[#50536452_pgfId-926349]##This annotation allows a customized mapping to
a XML Schema built in type. This is useful where a Java type can map to
more than one schema built in types. An example is
_XMLGregorianCalendar_ which can represent one of the eight schema
built-in types.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-926351]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-925202]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{FIELD, METHOD,
PACKAGE})

[#50536452_pgfId-925203]##public @interface XmlSchemaType \{

[#50536452_pgfId-925218]## String name();

[#50536452_pgfId-925219]## String namespace() default
"http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema";

[#50536452_pgfId-925220]## Class type() default DEFAULT.class;

[#50536452_pgfId-925216]## static final class DEFAULT \{}

[#50536452_pgfId-925205]##}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-926106]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-927944]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-927945]##name() must be an atomic simple type schema
type (or a type that derives from it) to which the type of the property
or field can be mapped from XML Schema -> Java as specified in Section
6.2.2, “Atomic Datatype”. Example

[#50536452_pgfId-926190]##

[#50536452_pgfId-926219]## // @XmlSchemaType can specify any one of the
eight calendar types

[#50536452_pgfId-926220]## // that map to XMLGregorianCalendar.

[#50536452_pgfId-926196]## @XmlSchemaType(name=”date”)

[#50536452_pgfId-926194]## XMLGregorianCalendar foo;

* [#50536452_pgfId-927937]## If the annotation is used as a package
level annotation or within _@XmlSchemaTypes_ , value of
_@XmlSchemaType.type()_ must be specified and must be the Java type that
is being customized.
* [#50536452_pgfId-927938]##If the annotation is used on a field or a
method, then value of type() must be DEFAULT.class.
* [#50536452_pgfId-928152]##This annotation can only be used with the
following other annotations: _@XmlElement, @XmlAttribute,
@XmlJavaTypeAdapter, @XmlJavaTypeAdapters._

[#50536452_pgfId-930790]##package:

[#50536452_pgfId-930791]##When this annotation is used at the package
level, the mapping applies to references to _@XmlSchemaType.type()_ as
specified below. For clarity, the following code example is used along
with normative text.

[#50536452_pgfId-930792]##// Example: change the default mapping at
package level

[#50536452_pgfId-930852]##package foo;

[#50536452_pgfId-930815]##@javax.xml.bind.annotation.XmlSchemaType

[#50536452_pgfId-930851]## (name="date",

[#50536452_pgfId-930855]##
type=javax.xml.datatype.XMLGregorianCalendar.class)

[#50536452_pgfId-930797]##A _@XmlSchemaType_ that is specified as a
package level annotation must apply at the point of reference as
follows:

. [#50536452_pgfId-930798]##a property/field within a class in package
(e.g _exmple.po)_ whose reference type is _@XmlSchemaType.type()_ . For
e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-930799]## // XMLGregorianCalendar will be mapped to XML
Schema type "date"

[#50536452_pgfId-930800]## XMLGregorianCalendar cal;

. [#50536452_pgfId-930801]##a property/field within a class in package
(e.g _exmple.po)_ , where _@XmlSchemaType.type()_ is used as a
parametric type. For e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-930930]## // Example: Following code maps to a
repeating element with

[#50536452_pgfId-930951]## // XML Schema type of "date".

[#50536452_pgfId-930931]## List<XMLGregorianCalendar> bar;

[#50536452_pgfId-930965]##property/field:

[#50536452_pgfId-930956]##A _@XmlSchemaType_ specified on the
property/field maps references to _@XmlSchemaType.type()_ as follows:

. [#50536452_pgfId-930989]##property/field is a single valued.

[#50536452_pgfId-930990]## // Maps XMLGregorianCalendar to XML Schema
type "date"”

[#50536452_pgfId-930991]## @XmlSchemaType(name=”date”)

[#50536452_pgfId-931002]## public XMLGregorianCalendar cal;

. [#50536452_pgfId-930960]##a property/field where
_@XmlSchemaType.type()_ is used as a parametric type. For e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-931004]## // Example: Following code maps to a
repeating element with

[#50536452_pgfId-931005]## // XML Schema type of "date".

[#50536452_pgfId-931029]## @XmlSchemaType(name="date")

[#50536452_pgfId-930961]## List<XMLGregorianCalendar> bar;

==== [#50536452_pgfId-930932]##@XmlSchemaTypes

[#50536452_pgfId-930933]##This annotation is a container annotation for
defining multiple _@XmlSchemaType_ annotations at the package level.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-927865]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-927874]## @Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{PACKAGE})

[#50536452_pgfId-927875]## public @interface XmlSchemaTypes \{

[#50536452_pgfId-927876]## // Collection of @\{@link XmlSchemaType}
annotations

[#50536452_pgfId-927879]## XmlSchemaType[] value();

[#50536452_pgfId-927869]## }

===== [#50536452_pgfId-927909]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-927913]##Each _@XmlSchemaType_ annotation in
_@XmlSchemaTypes.value()_ must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_35544[See @XmlSchemaType]”.

== [#50536452_pgfId-926280]##[#50536452_46828]##Java class

==== [#50536452_pgfId-903564]##[#50536452_84530]##@XmlType

[#50536452_pgfId-930695]## _@XmlType_ is used to map a Java class to a
schema type. The schema type is computed from its annotation element
values.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-905965]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-905967]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{TYPE})

[#50536452_pgfId-905960]##public @interface XmlType \{

[#50536452_pgfId-881991]## String name() default "##default";

[#50536452_pgfId-881996]## String[] propOrder() default \{""};

[#50536452_pgfId-887270]## String namespace() default "##default" ;

[#50536452_pgfId-926358]## Class factoryClass() default DEFAULT.class;

[#50536452_pgfId-926360]## static final class DEFAULT \{};

[#50536452_pgfId-926356]## String factoryMethod() default "";

[#50536452_pgfId-887271]##}

[#50536452_pgfId-930703]## 

===== [#50536452_pgfId-888416]##[#50536452_20836]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-902172]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-902245]##a class must be either be a top level class
or a nested static class.
* [#50536452_pgfId-929128]##a class must have a public or protected
no-arg constructor or a factory method identified by \{ _factoryClass(),
factoryMethod()_ } unless it is adapted using _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ .
* [#50536452_pgfId-931743]##If _factoryClass()_ is other than
DEFAULT.class, then _factoryMethod()_ must be specified (i.e. the
default value ““ cannot be used.)
* [#50536452_pgfId-931744]##If _factoryClass()_ is _DEFAULT.class_ and
_factoryMethod()_ is not ““, then _factoryMethod()_ be a method in this
class.
* [#50536452_pgfId-929130]##if _@XmlType.propOrder_ is not \{} or \{““},
then the set must include all of the properties and fields mapped to
particles as specified in:
* [#50536452_pgfId-919813]##link:jaxb.htm#50536452_71316[See
@XmlElement]”
* [#50536452_pgfId-919821]##link:jaxb.htm#50536452_35987[See
@XmlElements]”
* [#50536452_pgfId-919826]##link:jaxb.htm#50536452_42695[See
@XmlElementRef]”
* [#50536452_pgfId-919831]##link:jaxb.htm#50536452_15713[See
@XmlElementRefs]”
* [#50536452_pgfId-933199]## _@XmlType.propOrder_ must not include a
field or property annotated with _@XmlTransient._
* [#50536452_pgfId-933200]##if the class, subClass, derives from another
XML-bound class, baseClass directly or indirectly (other than
java.lang.Object), then the subClass must not contain a mapped property
or field annotated with _@XmlValue_ annotation.
* [#50536452_pgfId-925653]##If a class contains a mapped property or
field annotated with _@XmlValue_ annotation, then all other mapped
fields or properties in the class must be mapped to an XML attribute.
* [#50536452_pgfId-928659]##This annotation can be used with the
following annotations: _@XmlRootElement, @XmlAccessorOrder,
@XmlAccessorType._
* [#50536452_pgfId-930766]##Even though the syntax allows it, @XmlType
is disallowed on an interface.

[#50536452_pgfId-902250]##A class annotated with @ _XmlType_ , must be
mapped as specified below:

[#50536452_pgfId-893327]##class must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_59475[See Mapping: Class to Simple Type
Definition] if the class contains only one mapped property or field that
is annotated with @ _XmlValue_ as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_24636[See @XmlValue]”.

[#50536452_pgfId-893722]##otherwise, the class must be mapped as
specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536452_12211[See Mapping: Class to Complex
Type
Definition].[#50536452_63807]##[#50536452_ct-base_type_definition]##[#50536452_derivation_method]##[#50536452_ct-final]##[#50536452_ct-abstract]##[#50536452_ct-attribute_declarations]##[#50536452_ct-attribute_wildcard]##[#50536452_content_type]##[#50536452_ct-exact]##[#50536452_ct-annotations]##

======= [#50536452_pgfId-893728]##[#50536452_12211]##Mapping: Class to Complex Type Definition

[#50536452_pgfId-893732]##\{name}

==== [#50536452_pgfId-906129]##@XmlRootElement

[#50536452_pgfId-906130]## _@XmlRooElement_ can be used to associate a
global element with the schema type to which a class is mapped.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-888268]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-881567]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{TYPE}

[#50536452_pgfId-881592]##public @interface XmlRootElement \{

[#50536452_pgfId-881571]## String name() default "##default" ;

[#50536452_pgfId-881583]## String namespace() default "##default" ;

[#50536452_pgfId-881565]##}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-881564]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-888267]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

. [#50536452_pgfId-928205]##The only other annotations allowed with this
annotation are: _@XmlType, @XmlEnum, @XmlAccessorType,
@XmlAcessorOrder._

[#50536452_pgfId-928188]##A class annotated with _@XmlRootElement_
annotation, must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_37478[See Mapping: Class to Element Declaration].

_##default_ “ _,_ then the value of the targetNamespace to which the
package containing the class is mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_16334[See Mapping: Package to XML target
namespace]
