==== [#50536452_pgfId-907874]##@XmlTransient

[#50536452_pgfId-933227]## _@XmlTransient_ is used to prevent the
mapping of a class.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-933228]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-933237]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(TYPE)

[#50536452_pgfId-933238]##public @interface XmlTransient \{}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-933235]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-933260]##The class must not be mapped. Any reference to
this class from the other XML-bound classes will treated as if they are
refering to the nearest XML-bound ancestor of this class (which could be
_java.lang.Object_ , which guarantees that there always exists such a
class.)

[#50536452_pgfId-933262]##For the effect that this annotation causes on
derived classes, see link:jaxb.htm#50536452_12211[See Mapping: Class to
Complex Type Definition].

[#50536452_pgfId-933264]##Note that a class with _@XmlTransient_ may
still have properties and fields with JAXB annotations. Those are mapped
to XML when a derived class is mapped to XML. See section
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_51080[See Property And Field] for more details.

[#50536452_pgfId-933266]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-933268]## _@XmlTransient_ is mutually exclusive with
all other mapping annotations.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-933226]##@XmlSeeAlso

[#50536452_pgfId-933147]## _@XmlSeeAlso_ is an annotation that can be
optionally placed on a class to instruct the JAXB runtime and the schema
generator to also bind classes listed in _@XmlSeeAlso_ , when it binds
the class that _@XmlSeeAlso_ is on.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-933175]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-933181]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(TYPE)

[#50536452_pgfId-933182]##public @interface XmlRootElement \{

[#50536452_pgfId-933183]## Class[] value();

[#50536452_pgfId-933185]##}

==== [#50536452_pgfId-908243]##@XmlType

===== [#50536452_pgfId-908250]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-908256]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{TYPE})

[#50536452_pgfId-908257]##public @interface XmlType \{

[#50536452_pgfId-908258]## String name() default "##default";

[#50536452_pgfId-925584]## String namespace() default "##default" ;

[#50536452_pgfId-908259]## String[] propOrder() default \{""};

[#50536452_pgfId-925572]## Class factoryClass() default DEFAULT.class;

[#50536452_pgfId-925570]## static final class DEFAULT \{};

[#50536452_pgfId-925591]## String factoryMethod() default ““;

[#50536452_pgfId-908269]##}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-908270]##[#50536452_72931]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-932643]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

. [#50536452_pgfId-932644]## _factoryMethod(),factoryClass()_ and
_@XmlType.propOrder_ must be ignored.
. [#50536452_pgfId-931055]##This annotation can be used only with the
following other annotations: _@XmlRootElement, @XmlAccessorOrder,
@XmlAccessorType._ However, _@XmlAccessorOrder_ and _@XmlAccessorType_
must be ignored; they are not meaningful when used to annotate an enum
type.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-930599]##@XmlRootElement

[#50536452_pgfId-908831]## _@XmlRootElement_ can be used to associate a
global element with the schema type to which the enum type is mapped.

[#50536452_pgfId-931129]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

. [#50536452_pgfId-931130]##The only other annotations allowed with this
annotation are: _@XmlType, @XmlEnum, @XmlAccessorType,
@XmlAcessorOrder._ Note that _@XmlAccessorType_ and _@XmlAccessorOrder_
while allowed will be ignored by the constraint in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_72931[See Mapping].

[#50536452_pgfId-928553]##The mapping must be performed as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_54189[See Mapping: Enum type to Element
Declaration].

== [#50536452_pgfId-932213]##[#50536452_51080]##Property And Field

[#50536452_pgfId-932214]##The following must be mapped (subject to the
mapping constraints listed below):

* [#50536452_pgfId-932215]##read/write property as identified by
java.beans.Introspector.getBeanInfo with its nearest XML-bound
superclass as the stopClass.
* [#50536452_pgfId-899458]##non static, non transient field of all the
ancestors up to the stopClass (but excluding the stopClass itself); if
annotated with _@XmlAttribute_ , then static final field must be mapped
(informally this maps to a fixed attribute but this is formally
specified in the mapping tables below).

[#50536452_pgfId-933307]##A mapped property is a property found as above
and mapped either by default or using a JAXB annotation.

[#50536452_pgfId-933322]##A mapped field is a field found as above and
mapped either by default or using a JAXB annotation.

[#50536452_pgfId-925597]##A property or field that has been annotated
with _@XmlTransient_ is not mapped.

[#50536452_pgfId-920252]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced.

* [#50536452_pgfId-929244]##For a property, a given annotation can be
applied to either read or write property but not both.
* [#50536452_pgfId-932151]##A property name must be different from any
other property name in any of the super classes of the class being
mapped. +
* [#50536452_pgfId-929223]##A mapped field name or the de capitalized
name of a mapped property must be unique within a class. For e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-920241]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-920248]## // Example 1:

[#50536452_pgfId-920319]## // Both the field “x” and property getX/setX
are mapped by

[#50536452_pgfId-920320]## // default. However, the decapitalized name
property getX/setX

[#50536452_pgfId-920322]## // is also “x” which collides with the field
name “x”.

[#50536452_pgfId-920249]## public class Foo \{

[#50536452_pgfId-920250]## public int x;

[#50536452_pgfId-920315]##

[#50536452_pgfId-920251]## public int getX \{..};

[#50536452_pgfId-920327]## public void setX \{..};

[#50536452_pgfId-920303]## }

==== [#50536452_pgfId-920227]##[#50536452_71316]##@XmlElement

===== [#50536452_pgfId-861882]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-885312]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{FIELD, METHOD}

[#50536452_pgfId-885313]##public @interface XmlElement \{

[#50536452_pgfId-906296]## String name() default "##default" ; // name
for XML element

[#50536452_pgfId-906297]## boolean nillable() default false;

[#50536452_pgfId-931802]## boolean required() default false;

[#50536452_pgfId-906298]## String namespace() default "##default" ;

[#50536452_pgfId-906301]## Class type() default DEFAULT.class;

[#50536452_pgfId-921807]## String defaultValue() default "\u0000";

[#50536452_pgfId-906281]## static final class DEFAULT \{}

[#50536452_pgfId-885333]##}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-885304]##[#50536452_18781]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-931140]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-931141]##The only additional mapping annotations
allowed with _@XmlElement_ are: _@XmlID, @XmlIDREF, @XmlList,
@XmlSchemaType, @XmlValue, @XmlAttachmentRef, @XmlMimeType,
@XmlInlineBinaryData, @XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ and _@XmElementWrapper.
@XmlElement_ can also be used within _@XmlElements_ .
* [#50536452_pgfId-915651]##If the property or field type is a
parametric collection type, then _@XmlElement.type()_ must be
_DEFAULT.class_ or _collectionitem.class_ (since the type of the
collection is already known).

[#50536452_pgfId-902909]##A field or property annotated must be mapped
as follows:

* [#50536452_pgfId-919601]##If _@XmlElement.namespace()_ is not “
_##default_ ” and different from the _\{target namespace}_ of the
enclosing class, then it must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_78686[See Mapping: Property/field to Particle -
ref attribute].
* [#50536452_pgfId-929531]##If property is single valued, and it’s type
is annotated with _@XmlRootElement_ and _@XmlType.name()= ““_ , then the
property must be mapped as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536452_78686[See
Mapping: Property/field to Particle - ref attribute].

[#50536452_pgfId-930456]##Design Note: This mapping is designed to
eliminate an infinite recursion. For example:

[#50536452_pgfId-929611]## // Code fragment

[#50536452_pgfId-929628]## @XmlRootElement

[#50536452_pgfId-929612]## @XmlType(name="")

[#50536452_pgfId-929613]## class Foo \{

[#50536452_pgfId-929614]## Foo foo;

[#50536452_pgfId-930464]## }

[#50536452_pgfId-930465]##In the absence of the above mapping, the above
code would map to:

[#50536452_pgfId-930466]## <schema>

[#50536452_pgfId-929589]## <element name="foo">

[#50536452_pgfId-929555]## <complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-929556]## <sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-929557]## <element name=”foo” minOccurs=”0”>

[#50536452_pgfId-929662]## <complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-929644]## ... infinite recursion ...

[#50536452_pgfId-929559]##With the above mapping, the code fragment
would instead map to:

[#50536452_pgfId-929651]## <schema>

[#50536452_pgfId-929652]## <element name="foo">

[#50536452_pgfId-929653]## <complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-929654]## <sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-929657]## <element ref=”foo” minOccurs=”0”>

[#50536452_pgfId-929560]## 

* [#50536452_pgfId-929538]##otherwise, it must be mapped as
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_55059[See Mapping: Property/field to Particle -
no ref attribute].
* [#50536452_pgfId-886776]##

======= [#50536452_pgfId-886779]##Mapping: Property/field to [#50536452_78686]##Particle - ref attribute

[#50536452_pgfId-886783]##\{min occurs}

[#50536452_pgfId-931823]##if _@XmlElement.required()_ is true, then 1

[#50536452_pgfId-919696]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-931821]##if the property type is a primitive type or a
multi dimensional array with a primitive type then 1

[#50536452_pgfId-919697]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-915390]##otherwise 0

[#50536452_pgfId-886787]##\{max occurs}

[#50536452_pgfId-931488]##if the type of the property/field is not a
collection type, then 1

[#50536452_pgfId-902723]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-894014]##otherwise _unbounded_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-886791]##\{term}

[#50536452_pgfId-919723]##element declaration as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_93529[See Mapping: Property/field to Element
declaration] with the following overrides for the abstract schema
component properties:

[#50536452_pgfId-931898]##\{scope} is _global_

[#50536452_pgfId-931902]## _\{value constraint}_ is _absent_

[#50536452_pgfId-931917]## _\{type definition}_ is _xs:anyType_ if the
mapping results in two or more element decalarations with the same name.

[#50536452_pgfId-931960]##Note: The above make the element a global
element declaration rather than a local element declaration.

[#50536452_pgfId-919518]##

==== [#50536452_pgfId-914520]##[#50536452_35987]##@XmlElements

===== [#50536452_pgfId-915042]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-915048]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{FIELD,METHOD})

[#50536452_pgfId-915049]##public @interface XmlElements \{

[#50536452_pgfId-915053]## XmlElement[] value(); // collection of
@XmlElement annotations

[#50536452_pgfId-915046]##}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-915022]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-915599]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-915647]##If the property or field type is a
parameterized collection type, then the size of the
_@XmlElements.value()_ must be 1.
* [#50536452_pgfId-928304]##This annotation can be used only with the
following annotations: _@XmlIDREF, @XmlElementWrapper,
@XmlJavaTypeAdapter._
* [#50536452_pgfId-928241]##If _@XmlIDREF_ is specified, then each
_@XmlElement.type()_ must contain a JavaBean property/field annotated
with _@XmlID_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-915646]##The property or field must be mapped as
follows:

* [#50536452_pgfId-915643]##If the size of _@XmlElements.value()_ is 1,
then the property must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_71316[See @XmlElement]”.
* [#50536452_pgfId-915609]##otherwise it must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_23670[See Mapping: List of types to choice
particle].

[#50536452_pgfId-909435]##

===== [#50536452_pgfId-909611]##Synopsis

for XML element

===== [#50536452_pgfId-909637]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-909638]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-931601]##The only other additional JAXB mapping
annotations allowed with _@XmlElementRef_ are: _@XmlElementWrapper_ and
_@XmlJavaTypeAdapter._
* [#50536452_pgfId-931602]##If the collection item type or property type
(for single valued property) is _javax.xml.bind.JAXBElement_ , then \{
_@XmlElementRef.name()_ , _@XmlElementRef.namespace()}_ must point an
element factory method with an _@XmlElementDecl_ annotation in a class
annotated with _@XmlRegistry_ (usually _ObjectFactory_ class generated
by the schema compiler) :
* [#50536452_pgfId-913357]## _@XmlElementDecl.name()_ must equal
_@XmlElementRef.name()_
* [#50536452_pgfId-913381]## _@XmlElementDecl.namespace()_ must equal
_@XmlElementRef.namespace()_ .
* [#50536452_pgfId-913459]##If the collection item type (for collection
property) or property type (for single valued property) is not
_javax.xml.bind.JAXBElement_ , then the type referenced by the property
or field must be annotated with _@XmlRootElement_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-909631]##A field or property annotated with the
_@XmlElementRef_ annotation must be mapped as follows:

* [#50536452_pgfId-913478]##if the type of the property or field is
single valued property, then it must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_85834[See Mapping: Property/field (property type
single valued) to Particle with ref attribute]
* [#50536452_pgfId-913940]##otherwise (the type of the property or field
is a parametric type), then it must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_49723[See Mapping: Property/Field (parametric
type) to choice particle].

==== [#50536452_pgfId-909903]##@XmlElementWrapper

for XML element

===== [#50536452_pgfId-907001]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-914899]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-921875]##The only additional mapping annotations
allowed with _@XmlElementWrapper_ are: _@XmlElement, @XmlElements,
@XmlElementRef, @XmlElementRefs, @XmlJavaTypeAdapter._
* [#50536452_pgfId-921876]##The property or the field must be a
collection property.

follows:

* [#50536452_pgfId-922050]##If _@XmlElementWrapper.namespace()_ is not “
_##default_ ” and different from the _\{target namespace}_ of the
enclosing class, then it must be mapped as specified as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_36903[See Mapping: Property/field Element Wrapper
with ref attribute].
* [#50536452_pgfId-922056]##otherwise, it must be mapped as
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_57897[See Mapping: Property/field to Particle for
Element Wrapper].

==== [#50536452_pgfId-916858]##[#50536452_58593]##@XmlAttribute

[#50536452_pgfId-916773]## _@XmlAttribute_ is used to map a property or
a field to an XML attribute.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-881211]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-885147]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{FIELD, METHOD})

[#50536452_pgfId-885201]##public @interface XmlAttribute \{

[#50536452_pgfId-885203]## String name() default ##default”;

[#50536452_pgfId-918767]## boolean required() default false;

[#50536452_pgfId-918768]## String namespace() default "##default" ;

[#50536452_pgfId-918769]##}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-881212]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-902869]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-902870]##If the type of the field or the property is
a collection type, then the collection item type must be mapped to
schema simple type. Examples:

[#50536452_pgfId-919143]## @XmlAttribute List<Integer> foo; // legal

[#50536452_pgfId-919147]## @XmlAttribute List<Bar> foo; // illegal if
Bar does not map to a

[#50536452_pgfId-919148]## // schema simple type

* [#50536452_pgfId-917892]##If the type of the field or the property is
a non collection type, then the type of the property or field must map
to a simple schema type. Examples:

[#50536452_pgfId-919179]## @XmlAttribute int foo; // legal

[#50536452_pgfId-919180]## @XmlAttribute Foo foo; // illegal if Foo does
not map to a schema

[#50536452_pgfId-919181]## // simple type

* [#50536452_pgfId-919149]##The only additional mapping annotations
allowed with _@XmlAttribute_ are: _@XmlID, @XmlIDREF, @XmlList,
@XmlSchemaType, @XmlValue, @XmlAttachmentRef, @XmlMimeType,
@XmlInlineBinaryData, @XmlJavaTypeAdapter._
* [#50536452_pgfId-917921]##

[#50536452_pgfId-917916]##The property or field must be mapped as
follows:

* [#50536452_pgfId-917970]##If _@XmlAttribute.namespace()_ is not
“##default” and differs from the _\{target namespace}_ of the schema
type to which the type containing the property or field is mapped, then
the property or field must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_34009[See Mapping: Property/field to Attribute
Use (with ref attribute)].
* [#50536452_pgfId-918009]##otherwise, it must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_87273[See Mapping: Property/field to Attribute
Use (no ref attribute)].

[#50536452_pgfId-917725]## 

======= [#50536452_pgfId-918040]##[#50536452_34009]##Mapping: Property/field to Attribute Use (with ref attribute)

[#50536452_pgfId-918044]##\{required}

[#50536452_pgfId-918046]## _@XmlAttribute.required()_

[#50536452_pgfId-918048]##\{attribute declaration}

[#50536452_pgfId-918050]##attribute declaration whose \{name} is
_@XmlAttribute.name()_ and \{target namespace} is
_@XmlAttribute.namespace()._

[#50536452_pgfId-918051]##For e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-918052]## _<xs:attribute ref=”xml:lang”/>_

==== [#50536452_pgfId-898680]##[#50536452_24636]##@XmlValue

===== [#50536452_pgfId-888916]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-891730]## _@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{FIELD,
METHOD})_

[#50536452_pgfId-891728]## _public @interface XmlValue \{}_

===== [#50536452_pgfId-888918]##[#50536452_36843]##XmlValue Type Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-892324]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

. [#50536452_pgfId-894833]##At most one field or a property in a class
can be annotated with @ _XmlValue_ .
. [#50536452_pgfId-894834]## _@XmlValue_ can be used with the following
annotations:
. [#50536452_pgfId-926050]## _@XmlList_ - however this is redundant
since _@XmlList_ maps a type to a schema simple type that derives by
list just as _@XmlValue_ would.
. [#50536452_pgfId-931196]## _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_
. [#50536452_pgfId-893493]##If the type of the field or property is a
collection type, then the collection item type must map to a simple
schema type. Examples:

[#50536452_pgfId-918959]## // Examples (not exhaustive): Legal usage of
@XmlValue

[#50536452_pgfId-918960]## @XmlValue List<Integer> foo; // int maps to
xs:int

[#50536452_pgfId-918961]## @XmlValue String[] foo; // String maps to
xs:string

[#50536452_pgfId-918950]## @XmlValue List<Bar> foo; // only if Bar maps
to a simple

[#50536452_pgfId-918986]## // schema type

. [#50536452_pgfId-918914]##If the type of the field or property is not
a collection type, then the type of the property or field must map to a
schema simple type.
. [#50536452_pgfId-903025]##The containing class must not extend another
class (other than java.lang.Obect).

===== [#50536452_pgfId-918987]##Mapping

* [#50536452_pgfId-919111]##If the type of the property or field is a
collection type, then the type must be must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_40564[See @XmlValue: Mapping to list simple
type]”.
* [#50536452_pgfId-919121]##Otherwise, the schema type to which the type
of the property or field is mapped.

[#50536452_pgfId-919012]## 

======= [#50536452_pgfId-919016]##[#50536452_40564]##@XmlValue: Mapping to list simple type

[#50536452_pgfId-919022]##\{name}

[#50536452_pgfId-919024]## _absent_

[#50536452_pgfId-919036]##ur-type definition, _xs:anyType_ .

==== [#50536452_pgfId-888922]##[#50536452_34288]##@XmlID

===== [#50536452_pgfId-888840]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-891745]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{FIELD, METHOD})

[#50536452_pgfId-891740]##public @interface XmlID \{}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-894365]##XmlID Type Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-894372]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-894373]##at most one field or property in a class can
be annotated with _@XmlID_ .
* [#50536452_pgfId-929367]##The type of the field or property must be
_java.lang.String_ .
* [#50536452_pgfId-894374]##The only other program annotations allowed
with _@XmlID_ are: _@XmlAttribute_ and _@XmlElement_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-888911]##The type of the annotated program element must
be mapped to _xs:ID._

==== [#50536452_pgfId-888836]##[#50536452_24400]##@XmlIDREF

===== [#50536452_pgfId-888882]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-891757]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{FIELD, METHOD})

[#50536452_pgfId-888898]##public @interface XmlIDREF \{}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-888888]##XmlIDREF Type Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-894388]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-928108]##If the type of the field or property is a
collection type, then the collection item type must contain a property
or field annotated with _@XmlID_ .
* [#50536452_pgfId-928115]##If the field or property is not a collection
type, then the type of the property or field must contain a property or
field annotated with _@XmlID_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-931211]##Note: If the collection item type or the type
of the property (for non collection type) is _java.lang.Object,_ then
the instance must contain a property/field annotated with _@XmlID_
attribute.

* [#50536452_pgfId-928110]##The only additional mapping annotations
allowed with _@XmlIDREF_ are: _@XmlElement_ , _@XmlAttribute, @XmlList,_
and _@XmlElements, @XmlJavaTypeAdapter._

[#50536452_pgfId-892027]##If the type of the field or property is a
collection type, then each collection item type must be mapped to
_xs:IDREF_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-928136]##If the type of the field or property is single
valued, then the type of the property or field must be mapped to
_xs:IDREF_ .

==== [#50536452_pgfId-917031]##[#50536452_78561]##@XmlList

[#50536452_pgfId-917046]##This annotation maps a collection type to a
list simple type.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-917032]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-917033]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{FIELD, METHOD,
PARAMETER})

[#50536452_pgfId-917034]##public @interface XmlList \{}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-917035]##XmlIList Type Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-917036]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-917463]##The type of the field, property or parameter
must be a collection type.
* [#50536452_pgfId-931659]##The collection item type must map to a
simple schema type that does not derive by list. For example:

[#50536452_pgfId-918330]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-918334]## // Examples: Legal usage of @XmlList

[#50536452_pgfId-918739]## @XmlList List<Integer> foo; // int maps to
xs:int

[#50536452_pgfId-918336]## @XmlList String[] foo; // String maps to
xs:string

[#50536452_pgfId-918337]## @XmlList List<Bar> foo; // only if Bar maps
to a simple type

[#50536452_pgfId-918573]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-918749]## // Example: Illegal usage of @XmlList

[#50536452_pgfId-918577]## public class Foo \{

[#50536452_pgfId-918660]## // @XmlValue maps List to a XML Schema list
simple type

[#50536452_pgfId-918658]## @XmlValue List<Integer> a;

[#50536452_pgfId-918659]## }

[#50536452_pgfId-918560]## class Bar \{

[#50536452_pgfId-918666]## // Use of @XmlList is illegal since Foo
itself mapped

[#50536452_pgfId-918675]## // to a XML Schema list simple type; XML
Schema list simple

[#50536452_pgfId-918692]## // type can't derive from another XML Schema
list simple type

[#50536452_pgfId-918561]## @XmlList List<Foo> y;

[#50536452_pgfId-918547]## }

* [#50536452_pgfId-918728]##The only additional mapping annotations
allowed with _@XmlList_ are: _@XmlElement, @XmlAttribute, @XmlValue_ and
_@XmlIDREF, @XmlJavaTypeAdapter._

[#50536452_pgfId-918550]##The type of the property or field must be
mapped as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536452_69214[See @XmlList:
Mapping to list simple type].

[#50536452_pgfId-917060]##

== [#50536452_pgfId-918158]##ObjectFactory Method

[#50536452_pgfId-912643]##The annotations in this section are intended
primarily for use by schema compiler in annotating element factory
methods in the schema derived ObjectFactory class
(link:jaxb.htm#50536473_80810[See Java Package]”). They are not expected
to be used when mapping existing classes to schema.

[#50536452_pgfId-912662]## 

==== [#50536452_pgfId-912391]##@XmlElementDecl

===== [#50536452_pgfId-912395]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-912691]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{METHOD})

[#50536452_pgfId-912693]##public @interface XmlElementDecl \{

[#50536452_pgfId-912786]## Class scope() default GLOBAL.class;

[#50536452_pgfId-913006]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-913005]## // XML namespace of element

[#50536452_pgfId-912931]## String namespace() default "##default";

[#50536452_pgfId-913009]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-912992]## String name(); // local name of element

[#50536452_pgfId-912981]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-912725]## //XML namespace name of a substitution
group's head element.

[#50536452_pgfId-912745]## String substitutionHeadNamespace() default
"##default";

[#50536452_pgfId-913004]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-912747]## //XML local name of a substitution group's
head element.

[#50536452_pgfId-912755]## String substitutionHeadName() default "";

[#50536452_pgfId-912757]## public final class GLOBAL \{}

[#50536452_pgfId-912399]##}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-912400]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-912404]##The following mapping constraints must be
enforced:

* [#50536452_pgfId-912592]##annotation can only be used on an element
factory method (link:jaxb.htm#50536473_80810[See Java Package]”). The
annotation creates a mapping between an XML schema element declaration
and a element factory method that returns a _JAXBElement_ instance
representing the element declaration. Typically, the element factory
method is generated (and annotated) from a schema into the
_ObjectFactory_ class in a Java package that represents the binding of
the element declaration's target namespace. Thus, while the annotation
syntax allows _@XmlElementDecl_ to be used on any method, semantically
its use is restricted to annotation of element factory method
* [#50536452_pgfId-913010]##class containing the element factory method
annotated with _@XmlElementDecl_ must be annotated with _@XmlRegistry_ .
* [#50536452_pgfId-912626]##element factory method must take one
parameter assignable to _java.lang.Object_ .
* [#50536452_pgfId-920089]##two or more element factory methods
annotated with _@XmlElementDecl_ must not map to element declarations
with identical _\{name}_ _\{target namespace}_ values.
* [#50536452_pgfId-920088]##if type Foo has an element factory method
and is also annotated with @XmlRootElement, then they must not map to
element declarations with identical _\{name}_ and _\{target namespace}_
values.

[#50536452_pgfId-920069]##One example of where the above scenario occurs
is when a developer attempts to add behavior/data to code generated from
schema. For e.g. schema compiler generates an element instance factory
method (e.g. _createFoo_ ) annotated with _@XmlElementDecl_ . But the
developer annotates _Foo_ with _@XmlRootElement_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-912486]##An element factory method must be mapped as
specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536452_54475[See Mapping: Element Factory
method to Element Declaration].

[#50536452_pgfId-912405]## 

======= [#50536452_pgfId-912410]##[#50536452_54475]##Mapping: Element Factory method to Element Declaration

[#50536452_pgfId-912414]##\{name}

[#50536452_pgfId-912421]## _@XmlElementDecl.name()_

[#50536452_pgfId-912423]##\{target namespace}

{empty}[#50536452_pgfId-912425]##if _@XmlElementDecl.namespace()_ is “
_##default_ “ _,_ then the value of the targetNamespace to which the
package of the class containing the factory method is mapped as
specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536452_16334[See Mapping: Package to XML
target namespace]

[#50536452_pgfId-912429]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-912430]##otherwise _@XmlElementDecl.namespace()_

[#50536452_pgfId-912432]##\{type definition}

[#50536452_pgfId-912434]##schema type to which the class is mapped as
specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536452_84530[See @XmlType]”.

[#50536452_pgfId-912439]##\{scope}

[#50536452_pgfId-912575]## _global_ if _@XmlElementDecl.scope()_ is
_@XmlElementDecl.GLOBAL_

[#50536452_pgfId-912576]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-912507]##otherwise the complex type definition to which
the class containing the object factory method is mapped.

[#50536452_pgfId-912443]##\{value constraint}

[#50536452_pgfId-912445]## _absent_

[#50536452_pgfId-912447]##\{nillable}

[#50536452_pgfId-912449]## _false_

[#50536452_pgfId-912451]##\{identity-constraint definitions}

[#50536452_pgfId-912453]##empty set

[#50536452_pgfId-912455]##\{substitution group affiliation}

[#50536452_pgfId-912457]##element declaration derived from
_@XmlElementDecl.name()_ and _@XmlElementDecl.substitutionHeadName()_

[#50536452_pgfId-912460]##\{substitution group exclusions}

[#50536452_pgfId-912462]## _\{}_

[#50536452_pgfId-912464]##\{disallowed substitution}

[#50536452_pgfId-912544]##\{}

[#50536452_pgfId-912468]##\{abstract}

[#50536452_pgfId-912470]## _false_

[#50536452_pgfId-912473]##\{annotation}

[#50536452_pgfId-912475]## _unspecified_

== [#50536452_pgfId-912383]##Adapter

==== [#50536452_pgfId-900825]##XmlAdapter

[#50536452_pgfId-915420]##public abstract class
XmlAdapter<ValueType,BoundType> \{

[#50536452_pgfId-915423]## // Do-nothing constructor for the derived
classes.

[#50536452_pgfId-915425]## protected XmlAdapter() \{}

[#50536452_pgfId-915426]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-915428]## // Convert a value type to a bound type.

[#50536452_pgfId-915430]## public abstract BoundType unmarshal(ValueType
v);

[#50536452_pgfId-915431]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-915506]## // Convert a bound type to a value type.

[#50536452_pgfId-915508]## public abstract ValueType marshal(BoundType
v);

[#50536452_pgfId-915418]##}

link:jaxb.htm#50536452_29781[See Adapter]”.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-911812]##[#50536452_69143]##@XmlJavaTypeAdapter

===== [#50536452_pgfId-900827]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-911834]##@Retention(RUNTIME)
@Target(\{PACKAGE,FIELD,METHOD,TYPE,PARAMETER})

[#50536452_pgfId-911835]##public @interface XmlJavaTypeAdapter \{

[#50536452_pgfId-911839]## Class<? extends XmlAdapter> value();

[#50536452_pgfId-927825]## Class type() default DEFAULT.class;

[#50536452_pgfId-927823]## static final class DEFAULT \{}

[#50536452_pgfId-911832]##}

[#50536452_pgfId-897552]##For an overview, see
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_29781[See Adapter]”.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-930035]##Scope

[#50536452_pgfId-900676]##The scope of _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ must cover
the program elements as specified below:

[#50536452_pgfId-929817]##package:

[#50536452_pgfId-929830]##For clarity, the following code example is
used along with normative text.

[#50536452_pgfId-929823]##// Adapts Foo type to MyFoo type

[#50536452_pgfId-929855]##FooAdapter extends XmlAdapter<MyFoo, Foo>

[#50536452_pgfId-929860]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-929861]##// FooAdapter is installed at the package
level - example.po

[#50536452_pgfId-929864]##@XmlJavaTypeAdapter(value=FooAdapter.class,
type=Foo.class)

[#50536452_pgfId-929906]##A _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ that extends
_XmlAdapter <valueType, boundType>_ and is specified as a package level
annotation must adapt _boundType_ at the point of reference as follows:

. [#50536452_pgfId-929907]##a property/field/parameter within a class in
package (e.g _exmple.po)_ whose reference type is _boundType_ . For e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-929880]## // Foo will be adapted to MyFoo

[#50536452_pgfId-930086]## Foo foo;

. [#50536452_pgfId-930087]##a property/field/parameter within a class in
package (e.g _exmple.po)_ , where _boundType_ is used as a parametric
type. For e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-929919]## // List<Foo> will be adapted to List<MyFoo>

[#50536452_pgfId-929920]## Foo foo;

[#50536452_pgfId-927817]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-900807]##class, interface, enum type:

[#50536452_pgfId-930155]##For clarity, the following code example is
used along with normative text.

[#50536452_pgfId-930156]##// Adapts Foo type to MyFoo type

[#50536452_pgfId-930157]##FooAdapter extends XmlAdapter<MyFoo, Foo>

[#50536452_pgfId-930167]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-930176]##// FooAdapter is specified on class, interface
or enum type. @XmlJavaTypeAdapter(FooAdapter.class)

[#50536452_pgfId-930180]##public class Foo \{...}

[#50536452_pgfId-930111]##A _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ that extends
_XmlAdapter <valueType, boundType>_ and is specified on the class,
interface or Enum type (i.e. on a program element that matches meta
annotation @Target=\{type}) must adapt _boundType_ at the point of
reference as follows:

. [#50536452_pgfId-930131]##a property/field whose reference type is
_boundType_ . For e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-930132]## // Foo will be adapted to MyFoo

[#50536452_pgfId-930133]## Foo foo;

. [#50536452_pgfId-930134]##a property/field where _boundType_ is used
as a parametric type. For e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-930135]## // List<Foo> will be adapted to List<MyFoo>

[#50536452_pgfId-930227]## List<Foo> foo;

[#50536452_pgfId-930237]##Note: A _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ on a class does
not apply to references to it’s sub class.

[#50536452_pgfId-895643]##//Example:

[#50536452_pgfId-897069]##@XmlJavaTypeAdapter(..) public class Foo \{..}

[#50536452_pgfId-897998]##...

[#50536452_pgfId-898031]##public class DerivedFoo extends Foo \{..}

[#50536452_pgfId-898037]##...

[#50536452_pgfId-898005]##public class Bar \{

[#50536452_pgfId-898011]## // XmlJavaTypeAdapter applies to foo;

[#50536452_pgfId-898027]## public Foo foo;

[#50536452_pgfId-898040]## ...

[#50536452_pgfId-898015]## // XmlJavaTypeAdaper DOES NOT apply to
derivedFoo;

[#50536452_pgfId-898028]## public DerivedFoo derivedFoo;

[#50536452_pgfId-898007]##}

[#50536452_pgfId-930252]##property/field/parameter:

[#50536452_pgfId-930338]##A _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ that extends
_XmlAdapter <valueType, boundType>_ and is specified on the
property/field or parameter must adapt _boundType_ as follows:

. [#50536452_pgfId-930339]##property/field is a single valued and its
type is _boundType_ :

[#50536452_pgfId-930293]## // Foo will be adapted to MyFoo

[#50536452_pgfId-930297]## @XmlJavaTypeAdapter(FooAdapter.class) Foo
foo;

. [#50536452_pgfId-930319]##a property/field where _boundType_ is used
as a parametric type. For e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-930320]## // List<Foo> will be adapted to List<MyFoo>

[#50536452_pgfId-930324]## List<Foo> foo;

===== [#50536452_pgfId-929963]##Relationship to other annotations

[#50536452_pgfId-930039]## _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ must be applied first
before any other mapping annotation is processed. Further annotation
processing is subject to their respective mapping constraints. For
example,

[#50536452_pgfId-930040]##// PtoQAdapter is applied first and therefore
converts type Q to P

[#50536452_pgfId-930041]##// Next foo is mapped with a type of P (not Q)
subject to the

[#50536452_pgfId-930042]##// mapping constraints specified in
@XmlElements.

[#50536452_pgfId-930043]##@XmlJavaTypeAdapter(PtoQAdapter)

[#50536452_pgfId-930044]##@XmlElements(\{

[#50536452_pgfId-930045]## @XmlElement(name="x",type=PX.class),

[#50536452_pgfId-930046]## @XmlElement(name="y",type=PY.class)

[#50536452_pgfId-930047]##})

[#50536452_pgfId-930048]##Q foo;

[#50536452_pgfId-930049]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-930050]##@XmlType abstract class P \{}

[#50536452_pgfId-930051]##@XmlType class PX extends P \{}

[#50536452_pgfId-929931]##@XmlType class PY extends P \{}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-899660]##Class Inheritance Semantics

[#50536452_pgfId-897077]##When annotated on a class, the use of
_@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ annotation is subject to the class inheritance
semantics described here. The semantics is described in terms of two
classes: a _BaseClass_ and a _SubClass_ that derives from _BaseClass_ .
There are two cases to consider:

* [#50536452_pgfId-900917]## _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ annotates the
_BaseClass_
* [#50536452_pgfId-900921]## _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ annotates the
_SubClass_ , a class that derives from _BaseClass_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-900839]##BaseClass: In this case, _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_
annotates the _BaseClass_ . In this case, the marshalling and
unmarshalling of an instance of property or a field with a static type
of baseClass must follow the schema to which
_XmlJavaTypeAdapter.value()_ is mapped.

[#50536452_pgfId-895116]##//Example: code fragment

[#50536452_pgfId-901085]##@XmlJavaTypeAdapter(..) BaseClass \{..}

[#50536452_pgfId-895117]##public SubClass extends BaseClass \{..}

[#50536452_pgfId-895118]##public BaseClass foo;

[#50536452_pgfId-895119]##public SubClass subFoo = new SubClass();

[#50536452_pgfId-901074]##foo = subFoo;

[#50536452_pgfId-901075]##In the absence of _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_
annotation, the instance of subFoo is marshalled with an xsi:type:

[#50536452_pgfId-895125]##<foo xsi:type="subClass"/>

[#50536452_pgfId-903231]##With the _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ annotation,
however, the instance of subFoo must be marshalled/unmarshalled
following the XML schema for _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter.value()_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-903232]##Subclass: In this case, _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_
annotates the _SubClass_ . By definition, the annotation does not cover
references to BaseClass. Thus, the schema types to which _SubClass_ and
_BaseClass_ map are not in the same schema type hierarchy. Hence an
object with a static type of _BaseClass_ but containing an instance of
_SubClass_ can’t be marshalled or unmarshalled. An attempt to do so must
fail. For e.g,

[#50536452_pgfId-895133]##// Example: Code fragment

[#50536452_pgfId-899841]##BaseClass\{..}

[#50536452_pgfId-899842]##...

[#50536452_pgfId-895134]##@XmlJavaTypeAdapter(..) SubClass extends
BaseClass \{..}

[#50536452_pgfId-895135]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-895136]##public class Bar \{

[#50536452_pgfId-895137]## public BaseClass foo;

[#50536452_pgfId-895138]## public SubClass subFoo = new SubClass();

[#50536452_pgfId-899849]##

[#50536452_pgfId-899859]## // marshal, unmarshal of foo will fail

[#50536452_pgfId-899857]## foo = subFoo;

[#50536452_pgfId-900907]##

[#50536452_pgfId-900914]## // marshal, unmarshal of subFoo will succeed

[#50536452_pgfId-927962]##}

==== [#50536452_pgfId-927968]##@XmlJavaTypeAdapters

[#50536452_pgfId-928038]##This annotation is a container annotation for
defining multiple _@XmlJavTypeAdapters_ annotations at the package
level.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-927978]##Synopsis

[#50536452_pgfId-927984]##@Retention(RUNTIME) @Target(\{PACKAGE})

[#50536452_pgfId-927985]##public @interface XmlJavaTypeAdapters \{

[#50536452_pgfId-927986]## // Collection of @\{@link XmlJavaTypeAdapter}
annotations

[#50536452_pgfId-927989]## XmlJavaTypeAdapter[] value();

[#50536452_pgfId-927982]##}

===== [#50536452_pgfId-928013]##Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-928017]##Each _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ annotation in
_@XmlJavaTypeAdapters.value()_ must be mapped as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_69143[See @XmlJavaTypeAdapter]”.

== [#50536452_pgfId-927964]##[#50536452_90141]##Default Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-927965]##This section describes the default mapping of
program elements. The default mapping is specified in terms of default
annotations that are considered to apply to a program element even in
their absence.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-925389]##[#50536452_80178]##Java Identifier To XML Name

[#50536452_pgfId-925390]##The following is the default mapping for
different identifiers:

* [#50536452_pgfId-925391]##class name: a class name is mapped to an XML
name by de capitalization using
_java.beans.Introspector.decapitalize(class name )._
* [#50536452_pgfId-925392]##enumtype name: enumtype name is mapped to an
XML name by de capitalization using
_java.beans.Introspector.decapitalize(enumtype name)._
* [#50536452_pgfId-925393]##A property name (e.g. address) is derived
from JavaBean access method (e.g. getAddress) by JavaBean de
capitalization of the JavaBean property name
_java.beans.Introspector.decapitalize(JavaBeanAccessMethod)_

==== [#50536452_pgfId-925387]##Package

[#50536452_pgfId-910547]##A package must be mapped with the following
default package level mapping annotations:

* [#50536452_pgfId-912311]## _@XmlAccessorType( +
javax.xml.bind.annotation.XmlAccessType.PUBLIC_MEMBER)_
* [#50536452_pgfId-921139]## _@XmlAccessorOrder( +
javax.xml.bind.annotation.XmlAccessOrder.UNDEFINED)_
* [#50536452_pgfId-926973]##

* [#50536452_pgfId-912379]## _@XmlSchema_

==== [#50536452_pgfId-925402]##[#50536452_42295]##Class

[#50536452_pgfId-925412]##Unless _@XmlTransient_ annotation is present,
a class with a public or protected no-arg constructor must be mapped
with the following default mapping annotations: _@XmlType_ .

==== [#50536452_pgfId-921208]##[#50536452_66212]##enum type

[#50536452_pgfId-921209]##An enum type must be mapped with the following
default mapping annotations:

* [#50536452_pgfId-910503]##enum type declaration:

[#50536452_pgfId-910492]## @XmlType

[#50536452_pgfId-926047]## @XmlEnum

[#50536452_pgfId-912340]## enum type \{...}

* [#50536452_pgfId-912341]##each enum constant:

[#50536452_pgfId-912342]## @XmlEnumValue (enumConstatEnum.name())

==== [#50536452_pgfId-910490]##[#50536452_43320]##Property / Field

[#50536452_pgfId-914427]##If the value of _@XmlAccessorType.value()_ is
_javax.xml.bind.annotation.XmlAccessType.NONE_ , then

* [#50536452_pgfId-921083]##properties and fields, unless explicitly
annotated, must be considered to be annotated with _@XmlTransient_ .

[#50536452_pgfId-921058]##If the value of _@XmlAccessorType.value()_ is
_javax.xml.bind.annotation.XmlAccessType.PROPERTY_ , then

* [#50536452_pgfId-915243]##properties not explicitly annotated must be
mapped; fields, unless explicitly annotated, must be considered to be
annotated with _@XmlTransient._

[#50536452_pgfId-915290]##If the value of _@XmlAccessorType.value()_ is
_javax.xml.bind.annotation.XmlAccessType.FIELD_ , then

* [#50536452_pgfId-915291]##fields not explicitly annotated must be
mapped; properties, unless explicitly annotated, must be considered to
be annotated with _@XmlTransient._

[#50536452_pgfId-916977]##If the value of _@XmlAccessorType.value()_ is
_javax.xml.bind.annotation.XmlAccessType.PUBLIC_MEMBER,_ then

* [#50536452_pgfId-916989]##all properties and public fields, unless
annotated with _@XmlTransient_ , must be mapped.

[#50536452_pgfId-915322]##See javadoc for
_@javax.xml.bind.annotation.XmlAccessorType_ for further information on
inheritance rules for this annotation.

===== [#50536452_pgfId-914116]##Default Mapping

[#50536452_pgfId-914120]##A property name (e.g. address) must be derived
from JavaBean access method (e.g. getAddress) by JavaBean
decapitalization of the JavaBean property name
_java.beans.Introspector.decapitalize(JavaBeanAccessMethod)_

[#50536452_pgfId-914131]##A single valued property or field must be
mapped with the following default mapping annotation:

[#50536452_pgfId-910438]## _@XmlElement_

* [#50536452_pgfId-920967]##

[#50536452_pgfId-919896]##A property or field with a collection type
must be mapped by with the following default mapping annotation:

* [#50536452_pgfId-919900]##if the property or field is annotated with
_@XmlList_ , then the default mapping annotation is:

[#50536452_pgfId-919922]## @XmlElement

[#50536452_pgfId-919931]## 

* [#50536452_pgfId-931831]##otherwise the default mapping annotation is:

[#50536452_pgfId-931832]## @XmlElements( \{ @XmlElement(nillable=true)})

==== [#50536452_pgfId-931833]##Map

[#50536452_pgfId-927387]##By default, _java.util.Map<K,V>_ must be
mapped to the following anonymous schema type. The parameterized types K
and V must be mapped as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536452_11235[See
Type Arguments and Wildcards]”. The anonymous schema type is at the
point of reference.

[#50536452_pgfId-910629]##<!-- Default XML Schema mapping for Map<K,V>
-->

[#50536452_pgfId-910630]##<xs:complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-910631]## <xs:sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-910632]## <xs:element name="entry"

[#50536452_pgfId-932971]## minOccurs ="0" maxOccurs="unbounded">

[#50536452_pgfId-910633]## <xs:complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-932984]## <xs:sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-932985]## <xs:element name="key" type="xs:anyType"

[#50536452_pgfId-933006]## minOccurs="0"/>

[#50536452_pgfId-932986]## <xs:element name="value" type="xs:anyType"

[#50536452_pgfId-933007]## minOccurs="0"/>

[#50536452_pgfId-910637]## </xs:sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-910638]## </xs:complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-910639]## </xs:element>

[#50536452_pgfId-910677]## </xs:sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-910686]##</xs:complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-927396]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-932591]##<!-- Default XML Schema mapping for
Map<String, Integer>-->

[#50536452_pgfId-927397]##<xs:complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-927398]## <xs:sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-927399]## <xs:element name="entry"

[#50536452_pgfId-933015]## minOccurs="0" maxOccurs="unbounded">

[#50536452_pgfId-927400]## <xs:complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-927401]## <xs:sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-927402]## <xs:element name="key" type="xs:string"

[#50536452_pgfId-933020]## minOccurs="0"/>

[#50536452_pgfId-927403]## <xs:element name="value" type="xs:int"

[#50536452_pgfId-933026]## minOccurs="0"/>

[#50536452_pgfId-927404]## </xs:sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-927405]## </xs:complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-927406]## </xs:element>

[#50536452_pgfId-927407]## </xs:sequence>

[#50536452_pgfId-927394]##</xs:complexType>

[#50536452_pgfId-927368]##The mapping of Map can be customized using
_@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ annotation.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-929764]##Multidimensional Array

[#50536452_pgfId-915785]##By default, a multidimensional array must be
mapped to a complex type as follows. Note the table specifies a two
dimensional array mapping. If an array is more than two dimensions, then
the mapping is used recursively.

[#50536452_pgfId-915872]## 

======= [#50536452_pgfId-915877]##Mapping: Two dimensional array to Complex Type Definition

[#50536452_pgfId-915881]##\{name}

[#50536452_pgfId-915998]##If the basetype is a primitive type (e.g.
int[][]) or its corresponding wrapper class (e.g. Integer[][]), then the
name is basetype concatenated with “Array” (e.g. intArray).

[#50536452_pgfId-915995]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-915996]##otherwise if the basetype is a reference type
(e.g. Foo[][]), then the XML name to which the reference type is mapped
(e.g. foo) concatenated with “Array” (e.g. fooArray).

[#50536452_pgfId-915892]##\{target namespace}

[#50536452_pgfId-915894]##if the basetype is a primitive or its
corresponding wrapper class then "http://jaxb.dev.java.net/array"

[#50536452_pgfId-916014]## __  

[#50536452_pgfId-916015]##otherwise the namespace to which the reference
type is mapped (e.g. for Foo[][], the namespace of the XML type to which
Foo is mapped).

[#50536452_pgfId-915908]##\{base type definition}

[#50536452_pgfId-915916]## _xs:anyType_

[#50536452_pgfId-915918]##\{derivation method}

[#50536452_pgfId-915920]## _restriction_

[#50536452_pgfId-915924]##\{final}

[#50536452_pgfId-915926]## _#all_

[#50536452_pgfId-915930]##\{abstract}

[#50536452_pgfId-915934]##false

[#50536452_pgfId-915936]##\{attribute uses}

[#50536452_pgfId-915938]##empty set

[#50536452_pgfId-915943]##\{attribute wildcard}

[#50536452_pgfId-915945]##absent

[#50536452_pgfId-915947]##\{content type}

[#50536452_pgfId-915954]## _element-only content +
content model_ mapped as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536452_28967[See
Mapping: Two dimensional array to sequence model group]”.

[#50536452_pgfId-915959]##\{prohibited substitutions}

[#50536452_pgfId-915961]##Empty set

[#50536452_pgfId-915965]##\{annotations}

[#50536452_pgfId-915967]## _absent_

[#50536452_pgfId-916136]## 

== [#50536452_pgfId-916141]##[#50536452_28967]##Mapping: Two dimensional array to sequence model group

[#50536452_pgfId-916145]##\{compositor}

[#50536452_pgfId-916149]## _xs:sequence_

[#50536452_pgfId-916152]##\{particles}

[#50536452_pgfId-916154]##A repeating element defined as follows:

[#50536452_pgfId-916180]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-916181]## _<xs:element name="item" type=schematype
minOccurs="0" maxOccurs="unbounded" nillable="true"/>_

[#50536452_pgfId-916158]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-916159]##where schematype is the schema to which the
array’s component type is mapped (e.g. int[][], then “xs:int”; Foo[][]
then “foo” assuming Foo is mapped to the schema type foo.

[#50536452_pgfId-916165]##\{annotation}

[#50536452_pgfId-916167]## _unspecified_

== [#50536452_pgfId-915844]##Notes

[#50536452_pgfId-915787]##This section contains a collection of notes
intended to aid in the review of this version of the specification. They
are collected here in a separate section and referenced from possibly
multiple places elsewhere in the specification to make the specification
more compact.

==== [#50536452_pgfId-902622]##[#50536452_89542]##@XmlType: List simple type

[#50536452_pgfId-902641]##It is possible to map a homogenous collection
to a simple type with a variety of \{list}. [#50536452_52027]##For e.g.

[#50536452_pgfId-902626]##// Code fragment

[#50536452_pgfId-902627]##public class USStateList \{

[#50536452_pgfId-902628]## @XmlValue

[#50536452_pgfId-902629]## List <int> items;

[#50536452_pgfId-902630]##}

[#50536452_pgfId-902631]## 

[#50536452_pgfId-902632]##// schema fragment

[#50536452_pgfId-902633]##<xs:simpleType name=”USStateList”>

[#50536452_pgfId-902634]## <xs:list itemType=”int”/>

[#50536452_pgfId-902673]##<xs:simpleType>

[#50536452_pgfId-902665]##Other types which can be mapped to a list
simple type include: indexed property, single dimensional arrays.

=== [#50536471_pgfId-1011060]##Chapter

[#50536471_pgfId-1011680]##[#50536471_18537]##Compatibility

[#50536471_pgfId-1011681]##This section describes conformance
requirements for an implementor of this specification. A JAXB
implementation must implement these constraints, without exception, to
provide a predictable environment for application development and
deployment.

[#50536471_pgfId-1011066]##This section explicitly lists the high level
requirements of this specification. Additional requirements can be found
in other sections of this specification and the associated javadoc for
package _javax.xml.bind_ and its subpackages. If any requirements listed
here conflict with requirements listed elsewhere in the specification,
the requirements here take precedence and replace the conflicting
requirements.

[#50536471_pgfId-1011172]##A JAXB implementation must implement the
processing model specified in Appendix B,
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_22990[See Runtime Processing]”.

[#50536471_pgfId-1011661]##A JAXB implementation included in a product
that supports software development must support a schema generator. A
schema generator must support all the Java Types to XML Schema mapping
specified in Section 8, link:jaxb.htm#50536452_74620[See Java Types To
XML]”.

[#50536471_pgfId-1011666]##A JAXB implementation included in a product
that supports software development must support a schema compiler. All
operating modes of a schema compiler must support all the XML
Schema-to-Java bindings described in this specification. Additionally,
any operating mode must not implement a default binding for XML
Schema-to-Java bindings as an alternative to those specified in Section
6, link:jaxb.htm#50536464_69201[See Binding XML Schema to Java
Representations]” nor alternative interpretations for the standard
customizations described in Section 7, link:jaxb.htm#50536467_62091[See
Customizing XML Schema to Java Representation Binding].”

[#50536471_pgfId-1011202]##The default operating mode for a schema
compiler MUST report an error when extension binding declaration is
encountered. All operating modes for a schema compiler MUST report an
error if an invalid binding customization is detected as defined in
Section 7. An extension binding declaration must be introduced in the
following cases:

. [#50536471_pgfId-1011205]##to alter a binding customization that is
allowed to be associated with a schema element as specified in Section
7, link:jaxb.htm#50536467_62091[See Customizing XML Schema to Java
Representation Binding].”
. [#50536471_pgfId-1011207]##to associate a binding customization with a
schema element where it is disallowed as specified in Section 7,
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_62091[See Customizing XML Schema to Java
Representation Binding].”

[#50536471_pgfId-1011249]##The default operating mode for a schema
compiler MUST report an error when processing a schema that does not
comply with the 2001 W3C Recommendation for XML Schema, [XSD Part 1] and
[XSD Part 2].

[#50536471_pgfId-1011259]##A schema compiler MAY support non-default
operating modes for binding schema languages other than XML Schema.

[#50536471_pgfId-1011701]##A schema compiler MUST be able to generate
Java classes that are able to run on at least one Sun's Reference
Implementation of the J2SE Java Runtime Environment that is Java SE 5 or
higher.

[#50536471_pgfId-1011739]##A schema generator MAY support non-default
operating modes for mapping Java types to schema languages other than
XML Schema.

[#50536471_pgfId-1011568]##A Java platform configured with any JAXB 2.0
implementation MUST allow any JAXB 1.0 application, packaged as
specified by the JAXB 1.0 implementation used by the application, to run
as specified by the JAXB 1.0 specification. A JAXB 1.0 application uses
schema-derived classes generated by a JAXB 1.0 compliant schema compiler
and is distributed with the compatible JAXB 1.0 runtime implementation.
Unlike JAXB 2.0, JAXB 1.0 specified a tight coupling between a JAXB 1.0
implementation’s schema-derived code and the JAXB 1.0 implementation of
package _javax.xml.bind_ . The required processing model for a JAXB 1.0
schema compiler generated package is specified in
_javax.xml.bind.JAXBContext_ class javadoc under the heading _SPEC
REQUIREMENT_ .
