Platform, Rajiv Mordani

=== [#50536490_pgfId-1036744]##[#50536490_91575]##Appendix

[#50536490_pgfId-1038700]##[#50536490_22990]##Runtime Processing

== [#50536490_pgfId-1038711]##Introduction[#50536490_61275]##

[#50536490_pgfId-1049865]##Two of the important goals of JAXB 2.0 are
portability (for inclusion in J2SE) and handling of invalid XML content
(for e.g. schema evolution). These goals imply that a JAXB Provider must
be capable of marshalling and unmarshalling XML instances using JAXB
annotated classes derived using another JAXB Provider. To ensure
portable behavior of JAXB mapped classes across JAXB Providers requires
a specification of runtime processing model of the JAXB 2.0 binding
framework.

[#50536490_pgfId-1038729]##This appendix specifies the runtime
processing model of XML instances and requirements on JAXB 2.0
Provider's runtime. It differs from the documentation found elsewhere in
the specification/javadocs. Chapter 4,”Binding Framework” and the
javadocs for the package javax.xml.bind do describe the JAXB 2.0 binding
framework. But these are written from a JAXB 2.0 developer perspective
rather than from a JAXB 2.0 Provider perspective and thus do not
describe requirements on JAXB 2.0 Provider runtime. This was sufficient
for JAXB 1.0 since portability was not a goal for JAXB 1.0 and schema
derived implementation classes were coupled to the JAXB 1.0 Provider
runtime. However, this is insufficient for JAXB 2.0, where portability
and handling invalid XML content are goals.

== [#50536490_pgfId-1038746]##Scope and Conventions

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1038748]##Scope

[#50536490_pgfId-1048934]##This appendix describes marshalling and
unmarshalling.

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1038756]##Format

[#50536490_pgfId-1038758]##The specification uses the following for
specifying runtime behavior:

* [#50536490_pgfId-1038760]##XML Infoset, Second Edition,
http://www.w3.org/TR/xml-infoset augmented with attributes xsi:type and
xsi:nil that can be used by a document author.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039649]##XML Schema abstract schema component model.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039658]##JAXB defined annotations as needed

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1049199]##Notations

[#50536490_pgfId-1049200]##The following notations/conventions are used:

* [#50536490_pgfId-1049201]##For brevity, property is used but is used
to mean JavaBean property or a field.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1049204]##XML Infoset properties that are associated
with an information item are enclosed in [...], for e.g. AII.[local
name]. And program elements the constitute the Java representation to
which an information item are identified as for e.g. AII.valuetype.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039727]##AII: Attribute Information Item in XML
Infoset
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039728]##AII.[local name] : local name property in
infoset for AII
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039738]##AII.[namespace] : namespace property in
infoset for AII
* [#50536490_pgfId-1048490]##AII.[owner element] : owner element in
infoset for AII
* [#50536490_pgfId-1049229]##AII.[normalized value]: normalized value in
inforset for AII
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039743]##AII.property : JAXB property to which AII
is mapped. The property in in the java type to which AII.[owner element]
is mapped.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039801]##AII.valuetype: Java type representing the
XML serialized for AII.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039813]##AII.boundtype: Java type that is bound;
this differs from AII.valuetype only if JAXB property is associated with
a @XmlJavaTypeAdapter.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1049219]##AII.schematype : schema type to which AII
is bound statically using Java -> XML schema mapping rules.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1049221]##EII: Element Information Item in infoset
* [#50536490_pgfId-1049222]##EII.[local name] : local name property in
XML infoset for EII
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039947]##EII.[namespace] : namespace property in XML
infoset for EII
* [#50536490_pgfId-1049242]##EII.[children]: children property in XML
infoset for EII
* [#50536490_pgfId-1049251]##EII.[parent]: parent property in XML
infoset for EII
* [#50536490_pgfId-1049244]##EII.property : JAXB property to which EII
is mapped. The property is in the javatype to which EII.[parent] is
mapped.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039977]##EII.valuetype : java type representing the
XML serialized for EII
* [#50536490_pgfId-1039987]##EII.boundtype : java type that is bound;
this differs from EII.valuetype only if JAXB property is associated with
a @XmlJavaTypeAdapter.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1040033]##EII.schematype : schema type to which EII
is bound statically using java -> XML schema mapping rules.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1040060]##EII.xsitype : the xsi:type specified in the
XML instance by a document author. null if no xsi:type was specified.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1050483]##EII.xsinil : the xsi:nil specified in the
XML instance by a document author. null if no xsi:nil was specified.

== [#50536490_pgfId-1050484]##Unmarshalling

[#50536490_pgfId-1051243]##This section specifies the runtime behavior
and JAXB provider requirements related to unmarshalling. The
specification includes unmarshalling of invalid XML content in an XML
instance. +
 +
This section specifies only flexible, standard unmarshalling (flexible
because unmarshalling deals with invalid XML content). Other
unmarshalling modes will not be specified. Flexible unmarshalling
specified here must be supported by all JAXB Providers.

[#50536490_pgfId-1051244]##The unmarshalling methods in the binding
framework fall into the following categories:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1050622]##Unmarshal methods that do not take a
declaredType as parameter:

[#50536490_pgfId-1051292]## _javax.xml.bind.Unmarshaller.unmarshal_
(...) +
_javax.xml.bind.Binder.unmarshal_ (...) +

[#50536490_pgfId-1051304]## 

. [#50536490_pgfId-1050623]##Unmarshal methods that take a declaredType
as a parameter:

[#50536490_pgfId-1051321]## _javax.xml.bind.Unmarshaller.unmarshal_
(..., _java.lang.Class<T> declaredType_ ) +
_javax.xml.bind.Binder.unmashal_ (..., _java.lang.Class<T> declaredType_
)

[#50536490_pgfId-1051253]##The unmarshal methods that do not take
declaredType as parameter must be unmarshalled as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_99007[See Globally Declared Root Element]”.

[#50536490_pgfId-1051273]##The unmarshal methods that take a
_declaredType_ as a parameter must be unmarshalled as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_20111[See Declared Type]”.

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1038838]##[#50536490_99007]##Globally Declared Root Element

[#50536490_pgfId-1038840]##There are two ways that a root element can be
represented in Java representation:

* [#50536490_pgfId-1048686]##as an element instance factory method that
is generated in the public ObjectFactory class of a package when a
schema is compiled. An element instance factory method is annotated with
a

[#50536490_pgfId-1040240]##@XmlElementDecl annotation. For e.g.

[#50536490_pgfId-1040252]## public class ObjectFactory \{

[#50536490_pgfId-1038850]## @XmlElementDecl(...)

[#50536490_pgfId-1038852]## public JAXBElement<T> createFoo(T
elementValue);

[#50536490_pgfId-1038853]## ...

[#50536490_pgfId-1038854]## }

* [#50536490_pgfId-1040306]##as a type (either an enum type or a class)
that has been annotated with @XmlRootElement. For e.g.

[#50536490_pgfId-1038858]##

[#50536490_pgfId-1038859]## @XmlRootElement(...)

[#50536490_pgfId-1038860]## public class Foo \{...}

[#50536490_pgfId-1038862]##The unmarshalling of XML content results in a
content tree with a root that is an instance of either a _JAXBElement_
instance or a type that is annotated with _@XmlRootElement_ . The
content tree must be created as follows:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1038870]##lookup an element factory method in the
ObjectFactory class matching on:

[#50536490_pgfId-1040426]##EII.[namespace] ==
@XmlElementDecl.namespace() && EII.[local name] ==
@XmlElementDecl.name()

[#50536490_pgfId-1040481]##or for a type annotated with @XmlRootElement
matching on:

[#50536490_pgfId-1040482]##EII.[namespace] ==
@XmlRootElement.namespace() && EII.[local name] ==
@XmlRootElement.name()

[#50536490_pgfId-1040574]##NOTE: The lookup will only find one of the
above not both. If both a type as well as an element factory method were
found, it would be flagged as an error when JAXBContext is created.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1040575]##if an element factory method in the
ObjectFactory class or a type annotated with @XmlRootElement is found,
then determine the valueType.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1040585]##if an element factory method is found,
there is no @XmlJavaTypeAdapter associated with the value parameter to
the element factory method, then the valueType is the java type of the
value parameter to the element factory method. For e.g.

[#50536490_pgfId-1038893]## @XmlElementDecl(name = "bar", namespace =
"")

[#50536490_pgfId-1038895]## public JAXBElement<Foo> createBar(Foo value)
\{

[#50536490_pgfId-1038896]## return new JAXBElement<Foo>(

[#50536490_pgfId-1040664]## _Bar_QNAME, ((Class) Foo.class), null,
value);

[#50536490_pgfId-1038897]## }

[#50536490_pgfId-1048571]##the valueType type is Foo.

* [#50536490_pgfId-1048732]##

[#50536490_pgfId-1048582]##if the parameter is associated with
@XmlJavaTypeAdapter, then the valueType is the java type specified in
@XmlJavaTypeAdapter.value() .

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048572]##if a type annotated with @XmlRootElement is
found then valueType is the type. For e.g.

[#50536490_pgfId-1038904]## @XmlRootElement(...)

[#50536490_pgfId-1038905]## public class Foo \{ ... }

* [#50536490_pgfId-1038907]##

[#50536490_pgfId-1038910]##Go to step 4, “Check for type substitution”

. [#50536490_pgfId-1040793]##If neither the element factory method nor a
type annotated with @XmlRootElement is found, then the element is
unknown. Set valueType of the element to null.

[#50536490_pgfId-1049273]##Even though the element is unknown, a
document author can still perform type substitution. This case can arise
if the XML schema contains only schema types and no global elements. For
e.g a document author could have specified a xsi:type that has been
mapped by JAXB. For e.g.

[#50536490_pgfId-1049266]## <unknownElement xsi:type="PurchaseOrder"/>

[#50536490_pgfId-1049276]##So goto step 4, "Check for type substitution"

. [#50536490_pgfId-1038927]##“Check for type substitution”
. [#50536490_pgfId-1040897]##if xsi:type is not specified, and the
valueType is null (i.e. the root element is unknown and we got to this
step from step 3), throw a _javax.xml.bind.UnmarshalException_ and
terminate processing.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1040950]##otherwise, if _xsi:type_ is specified, but
is not mapped to a JAXB mapped type (e.g. class is not marked with
@XmlType declaration), then throw a _javax.xml.bind.UnmarshalException_
and terminate processing.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1040997]##otherwise, if xsi:type is specified, and is
mapped to a JAXB mapped type set the valueType to the javatype to which
xsi:type is mapped.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1049998]##otherwise, xsi:type is not specified;
valueType is unchanged.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1052938]##Unmarshal valueType as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_89599[See Value Type]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1052939]##If the element factory method is annotated
with @XmlJavaTypeAdapter, then convert the valueType into a boundType

[#50536490_pgfId-1051025]## boundType =
@XmlJavaTypeAdapter.value().unmarshal(valueType)

. [#50536490_pgfId-1051026]##Determine the content root type to be
returned by unmarshal() method.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1051027]##if the element lookup returned an element
instance factory method, then create a JAXBElement instance using the
boundType. The content root type is the JAXBElement instance.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1051028]##otherwise, if the element lookup returned a
type annotated with @XmlRootElement, then the content root type is the
boundType.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1051029]##otherwise, the element is an unknown
element. Wrap the boundType using JAXBElement with an element name in
the XML instance document (e.g. “unknown Element”). The content root
type is the JAXBElement instance.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1051022]##return the content root type.

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1049999]##[#50536490_20111]##Declared Type

[#50536490_pgfId-1050643]##The unmarshalling process described in this
section must be followed for the unmarshal methods that take a
_declaredType_ as a parameter.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1050716]##Determine the valueType to be unmarshalled
as follows:
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050662]##if _xsi:type_ is specified, but is not
mapped to a JAXB mapped type , then throw a
_javax.xml.bind.UnmarshalException_ and terminate processing.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050735]##otherwise if _xsi:type_ is specified and is
mapped to JAXB mapped type, then valueType is the JAXB mapped type.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050739]##otherwise valueType is the argument passed
to _declaredType_ parameter in the +
_unmarshal_ (..., _java.lang.Class<T>declaredType_ ) call.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050715]##Unmarshal valueType as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_89599[See Value Type]”.

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1050642]##[#50536490_89599]##Value Type

[#50536490_pgfId-1050567]##The following steps unmarshal either
EII.valuetype or AII.valuetype, depending upon whether an EII or AII is
being unmarshalled.

[#50536490_pgfId-1052148]##Note: Whether an EII or AII is being
unmarshalled is determined by the “caller” of this section.
AII.valuetype and EII.valuetype are assumed to be set by the time this
section entered.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1052149]##If an instance of valueType does not exist,
create an instance of valueType as follows (for e.g. if a value of a
property with type _java.util.List_ is non null, then unmarshal the
value into that _java.util.List_ instance __ rather than creating a new
instance of _java.util.List_ and assigning that to the property):
. [#50536490_pgfId-1052150]##if valueType is a class and is the type
parameter specified in the element factory method, then instantiate the
class using element factory method; otherwise instantiate the class
using factory method if specified by _@XmlType.factoryClass()_ and
_@XmlType.factoryMethod();_ or if there is no factory method, using the
no-arg constructor.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1052134]##if valueType is an enum type, then obtain
an instance of the enum type for the enum constant annotated with
_@XmlEnumValue_ and _@XmlEnumValue.value()_ matches the lexical
representation of the EII.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1052135]##Invoke any event callbacks in the following
order as follows:
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050155]##If valueType implements an unmarshal event
callback _beforeUnmarshal(..)_ as specified in Section 4.4.1,”Unmarshal
Event Callback”, then invoke _beforeUnmarshal(..)_ .
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050165]##If _Unmarshaller.getListener()_ returns
_Unmarshaller.Listener_ that is not null, then invoke
_Unmarshaller.Listener.beforeUnmarshal(..)_ .
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050973]##If an EII.valuetype is being unmarshalled,
unmarshal into this instance the following. Note: The following steps
can be done in any order; the steps are just broken down and listed
separately for clarity:

[#50536490_pgfId-1050986]##If EII.valueType being unmarshalled

. [#50536490_pgfId-1050974]##unmarshal each child element information
item in EII.[children] as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_76619[See
Element Information Item]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1041210]##unmarshal each attribute information item
in EII.[attributes] as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_42383[See
Attribute Information Item]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1051382]##Unmarshal the value of EII.schematype or
AII.schematype following the Java to XML Schema rules defined in Chapter
8, “Java Types to XML”. If the value in XML instance is unparseable,
then it must be handled as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_17125[See
Unparseable Data for Simple types]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050178]##Invoke any event callbacks in the following
order as follows:
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050179]##If valueType implements an unmarshal event
callback _afterUnmarshal(..)_ as specified in Section 4.4.1,”Unmarshal
Event Callback”, then invoke _afterUnmarshal(..)_ .
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050199]##If _Unmarshaller.getListener()_ returns
_Unmarshaller.Listener_ that is not null, then invoke
_Unmarshaller.Listener.afterUnmarshal(..)_ .
. [#50536490_pgfId-1051158]##return // either AII.valuetype or
EII.valuetype.

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1038982]##[#50536490_76619]##Element Information Item

[#50536490_pgfId-1038984]##An EII must be unmarshalled as follows:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1041418]##infer EII.property as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_24480[See Property Inference - Element
Information Item]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050921]##if EII.property is null, then there is no
property to hold the value of the element. If validation is on (i.e.
Unmarshaller.getSchema() is not null), then report a
javax.xml.bind.ValidationEvent. Otherwise, this will cause any unknown
elements to be ignored.

[#50536490_pgfId-1053058]##If EII.property is not null and there is no
setter method as specified in section link:jaxb.htm#50536490_98148[See
Getters/Setters]” then report a javax.xml.bind.ValidationEvent.

[#50536490_pgfId-1050925]##Goto step 8.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1050928]##infer the EII.valuetype as described in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_87855[See Type Inference - Element Information
Item]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1041490]##if EII.valuetype is null, then go to step
8.

[#50536490_pgfId-1050950]##NOTE: EII.valuetype = null implies that there
was problem. so don't attempt to unmarshal the element.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1050951]##Unmarshal EII.valuetype as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_89599[See Value Type]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1042521]##if there is a @XmlJavaTypeAdapter
associated with EII.property, then adapt the EII.valuetype as follows:

[#50536490_pgfId-1039019]## EII.boundtype = +
@XmlJavaTypeAdapter.value().unmarshal(EII.valuetype)

[#50536490_pgfId-1039021]##otherwise

[#50536490_pgfId-1039023]##EII.boundtype = EII.valuetype

. [#50536490_pgfId-1039024]##set the value of EII.property to
EII.boundtype as follows:

[#50536490_pgfId-1042637]##Wrap EII.boundtype into a
javax.xml.bind.JAXBElement instance if:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048805]##the property is not a collection type and
its type is javax.xml.bind.JAXBElement
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048815]##the property is a collection type and is a
collection of JAXBElement instances (annotated with @XmlElementRef or
@XmlElementRefs)

[#50536490_pgfId-1048798]##If EII.property is not a collection type:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048816]##set the value of EII.property to
EII.boundtype.

[#50536490_pgfId-1048820]##If EII.property is collection type:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1042657]##add EII.boundtype to the end of the
collection.

[#50536490_pgfId-1039041]##NOTE: Adding JAXBElement instance or a type
to the end of the collection preserves document order. And document
order could be different from the order in XML Scheme if the instance
contains invalid XML content.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048200]##return

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1048247]##[#50536490_42383]##Attribute Information Item

[#50536490_pgfId-1039147]##An attribute information item must be
unmarshalled as follows:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1043166]##infer AII.property as described in section
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_21710[See Property Inference - Attribute
Information Item]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1053030]##if AII.property is null, then the attribute
is invalid with respect to the XML schema. This is possible if for e.g.
schema has evolved. If validation is on (i.e. Unmarshaller.getSchema()
is not null), then report a javax.xml.bind.ValidationEvent. Otherwise,
this will cause any unknown elements to be ignored.

[#50536490_pgfId-1053031]##If AII.property is not null and there is no
setter method as specified in section link:jaxb.htm#50536490_98148[See
Getters/Setters]” then report a javax.xml.bind.ValidationEvent. +
 +
Goto step 8.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1051044]##infer the AII.valuetype as described in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_70343[See Type Inference - Attribute Information
Item]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1051046]##if AII.valuetype is null, then go to step
8.

[#50536490_pgfId-1051047]##NOTE: AII.valuetype = null implies that there
was problem. so don't attempt to unmarshal the attribute.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1051073]##Unmarshal AII.valuetype as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_89599[See Value Type]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1043331]##If AII.property is associated with a
_@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ , adapt AII.valuetype as follows:

[#50536490_pgfId-1039169]## AII.boundtype =

[#50536490_pgfId-1045387]##
@XmlJavaTypeAdapter.value().unmarshal(AII.valuetype)

[#50536490_pgfId-1039172]##otherwise

[#50536490_pgfId-1051121]## AII.boundtype = AII.valuetype

. [#50536490_pgfId-1051128]##If AII.property is single valued:
. [#50536490_pgfId-1051129]##set the value of AII.property to
AII.boundtype.

[#50536490_pgfId-1051130]##If AII.property is a collection type (e.g.
List<Integer> was mapped to a Xml Schema list simple type using @XmlList
annotation):

[#50536490_pgfId-1051126]##add EII.boundtype to the end of the
collection.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1051762]##return[#50536490_14000]##

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1051769]##Property Inference

[#50536490_pgfId-1039195]##Unmarshalling requires the inference of a
property or a field that contains the value of EII and AII being
unmarshalled.

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1043556]##[#50536490_24480]##Property Inference - Element Information Item

[#50536490_pgfId-1039200]##The property to which an EII is mapped is
inferred based on name.

* [#50536490_pgfId-1048160]##

[#50536490_pgfId-1039208]##Infer EII.property by matching constraints
described below:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1049039]##initialize EII.property to null
. [#50536490_pgfId-1050854]##if property is mapped to XML Schema element
declaration, elem, in the content model of EII.[parent].schematype &&
EII.[local name] == elem.\{name} && EII.[namespace] == elem.\{namespace}

[#50536490_pgfId-1050855]##set EII.property to property

[#50536490_pgfId-1050856]## Goto step 4.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1043778]##If there is a JAXB property mapped to XML
Schema wildcard ( _xs:any_ ) (as determined by _@XmlAnyElement_ ), set
this JAXB property to EII.property. This property will hold wildcard
content (e.g. invalid XML content caused by schema evolution).
. [#50536490_pgfId-1043807]##return EII.property

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1039231]##[#50536490_21710]##Property Inference - Attribute Information Item

[#50536490_pgfId-1039233]##Infer the property for the AII by matching
constraints described below:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1043845]##initialize AII.property to null
. [#50536490_pgfId-1043856]##if property mapped to XML Schema attribute
declaration, attr, in the content model of AII.[owner].schematype &&
AII.[local name] == attr.\{name} && AII.[namespace] == attr.\{namespace}

[#50536490_pgfId-1043913]##set AII.property to property

[#50536490_pgfId-1043939]##Goto step 4.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1051661]##if there is a property mapped to a XML
Schema xs:anyAttribute (i.e. annotated with _@XmlAnyAttribute_ ), then
set this property to AII.property. This property holds XML content
matching wildcard attribute ( _xs:anyAttribute)_ or unknown attributes
(which can occur for e.g. if schema has evolved).
. [#50536490_pgfId-1051695]##return AII.property

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1051697]##Type Inference

[#50536490_pgfId-1048313]##Unmarshalling requires the inference of the
type of a property or a field that to contain the value of EII and AII
being unmarshalled.

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1048255]##[#50536490_87855]##Type Inference - Element Information Item

[#50536490_pgfId-1048257]##This section describes how to infer
EII.valuetype; this holds the value of the element (content model +
attributes).

[#50536490_pgfId-1048341]##EII.valuetype must be inferred as described
below:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048259]##initialize EII.valuetype to null.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048260]##if EII.xsitype is set, document author has
performed type substitution.

[#50536490_pgfId-1048261]##Goto step 4 to handle type substitution.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048262]##if EII.schematype is not mapped to a java
type, then
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048263]##report a validation event.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048264]##Go to step 7.

[#50536490_pgfId-1048265]##otherwise

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048266]##set EII.valuetype to the javatype to which
EII.schematype is mapped.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048267]##Go to step 7.

[#50536490_pgfId-1048268]##NOTE: This case can arise for example, when
EII.schematype is compiled into a java type at schema compilation time,
but the javatype was not registered with _JAXBContext.newInstance(..)_ .

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048269]##check if EII.xsitype is mapped to a JAXB
mapped type. It is possible that EII.xsitype is compiled to a javatype
at schema compilation time, but the javatype was not registered with
_JAXBContext.newInstance(..)_

[#50536490_pgfId-1048270]##If EII.xsitype is not mapped, then report a
validation event.

[#50536490_pgfId-1048271]##Goto step 7.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048276]##check if the java type to which EII.xsitype
is mapped is assignment comparable with the static type of the
property/field if no _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ is associated with the
property/field or with the _valueType_ specified in
_XmlAdapter<valueType, boundType>_ if a _@XmlJavaTypeAdapter_ is
associated with the property/field.

[#50536490_pgfId-1051541]##The above check can fail for e.g when a
document author attempts to substitute a complex type that derives from
simple type but customization to enable simple type substitution was not
used. For e.g.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048277]##<!-- local element with simple type -->

[#50536490_pgfId-1048278]## <xs:element name="foo" type="xs:int"/>

[#50536490_pgfId-1048279]## <!-- complex type for substituting the
simple type -->

[#50536490_pgfId-1048280]## <xs:complexType name="MyInt">

[#50536490_pgfId-1048281]## <xs:extension xs:int>

[#50536490_pgfId-1048282]## ...add attributes

[#50536490_pgfId-1048283]## </xs:extends>

[#50536490_pgfId-1048284]## </xs:complexType>

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048285]##customization to handle type substitution
of simple types is not used. So the property is

[#50536490_pgfId-1048286]## public int getFoo();

[#50536490_pgfId-1048287]## public void setFoo(int );

[#50536490_pgfId-1048288]## public class MyInt \{...}

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048289]##the document author attempts to substitute
complexType MyInt.

[#50536490_pgfId-1048290]## <foo xsi:type="MyInt"/>

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048291]##The type MyInt is not assignment comparable
with int.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048292]##set EII.valuetype to javatype to which
EII.xsitype is mapped.

[#50536490_pgfId-1048293]##NOTE: if we got to this step, this implies
that type substitution is valid.

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048294]##return EII.valuetype

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1048295]##[#50536490_70343]##Type Inference - Attribute Information Item

[#50536490_pgfId-1048296]##Infer the AII.valuetype as follows:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048297]##initialize AII.valuetype to null.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048298]##if AII.schematype is not mapped to a java
type, then report a validation event. Otherwise, set AII.valuetype to
the java type to which AII.schematype is mapped.

[#50536490_pgfId-1048299]##NOTE: This case can arise for example, when
AII.schematype is compiled into a java type at schema compilation time,
but the javatype is not registered with the
_JAXBContext.newInstance(..)_

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048300]##return AII.valuetype

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1048252]##Invalid XML Content

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1049047]##[#50536490_17125]##Unparseable Data for Simple types

[#50536490_pgfId-1050425]##If simple type data cannot be parsed into a
java datatype, then the value of the java datatype must not change the
current set value. An access to the datatype must return the value as
specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_64834[See Missing element
information item]”. If the conversion of lexical representation into a
value results in an exception, then the exception must be caught and a
validation event reported. This is to ensure that such conversion errors
do not terminate unmarshalling.

[#50536490_pgfId-1050429]##// Example : XML Schema fragment

[#50536490_pgfId-1050430]##<xs:element name="foo" type="xs:int"/>

[#50536490_pgfId-1050422]## 

[#50536490_pgfId-1050343]##// Example: XML instance.

[#50536490_pgfId-1050416]##// Data is not parseable into type xs:int ;
however unmarshal will

[#50536490_pgfId-1050417]##// still succeed.

[#50536490_pgfId-1050355]##<foo> SUN </foo>

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1050213]##[#50536490_64834]##Missing element information item

[#50536490_pgfId-1039266]##This case arises when an element declaration
required by a XML schema is missing from the XML instance.

[#50536490_pgfId-1039269]##Property or field access must return the
value specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_98174[See Value for missing
elements/attributes]”

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1039272]##Missing Attribute

[#50536490_pgfId-1039274]##This case arises when a property or a field
is mapped to an XML attribute but the attribute is missing from the XML
instance.

[#50536490_pgfId-1039277]##Property or field access must return the
value specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_98174[See Value for missing
elements/attributes]”.

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1039280]##[#50536490_98174]##Value for missing elements/attributes

[#50536490_pgfId-1039282]##If an attribute or an element is missing from
an XML instance, then unmarshal will not change the current set value.
An access to the property will return the set value or if unset, the
uninitialized value. The uninitialized value of the property or field
depends upon it's type. If the type is

. [#50536490_pgfId-1039288]##int - value is 0
. [#50536490_pgfId-1044117]##boolean - value is false
. [#50536490_pgfId-1044126]##a reference (must be mapped to a simple
type) - value is null.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1049340]##float - the value is +0.0f
. [#50536490_pgfId-1049774]##double - the value is 0.0d
. [#50536490_pgfId-1049775]##short - the value is (short) 0
. [#50536490_pgfId-1049776]##long - the value is 0L

[#50536490_pgfId-1049357]##Note The uninitialized values are returned
only if the value is not set. A value could be set for example in a
validation handler that catches the validation event.

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1039297]##[#50536490_26391]##Unknown Element

[#50536490_pgfId-1051488]##In this case, XML instance contains EII for
which there is no corresponding element declaration in the XML schema.
If the valuetype to which the EII.parent maps contains a property/field
annotated with _@XmlAnyElement_ , this EII can be unmarshalled into the
property/field.

[#50536490_pgfId-1051489]##Unknown attribute handling during
unmarshalling is specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_24480[See Property
Inference - Element Information Item]”.

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1051490]##Unknown attribute

[#50536490_pgfId-1050811]##In this case, XML instance contains AII for
which there is no corresponding attribute declaration in the XML schema.
If the valuetype to which the AII.parent maps contains a property/field
annotated with _@XmlAnyAttribute_ , the AII can be unmarshalled into the
property/field.

[#50536490_pgfId-1051416]##Unknown attribute handling during
unmarshalling is specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_21710[See Property
Inference - Attribute Information Item]”.

== [#50536490_pgfId-1039316]##Marshalling

[#50536490_pgfId-1045493]##To marshal a content tree, a JAXB application
invokes one of the following marshal methods:

[#50536490_pgfId-1045494]##Marshaller.marshal(Object jaxbElement, ...)
throws JAXBException;

[#50536490_pgfId-1051616]## 

[#50536490_pgfId-1051617]##Binder.marshal(Object jaxbObject, ...) throws
JAXBException;

[#50536490_pgfId-1046971]##A JAXB Provider must marshal the content tree
as follows:

* [#50536490_pgfId-1047699]##marshal the XML root element tag as
specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_53178[See XML Root Element Tag]”
* [#50536490_pgfId-1047701]##marshal _obj_ as specified in section
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_22516[See Type]”.

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1047703]##[#50536490_53178]##XML Root Element Tag

. [#50536490_pgfId-1047245]##If _obj_ is an instance of
_javax.xml.bind.JAXBElement_ then marshal _obj_ as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_59502[See JAXBElement]”

[#50536490_pgfId-1047855]##Goto step 4

. [#50536490_pgfId-1047856]##If _obj.getClass()_ is annotated with
_@XmlRootElement_ , then set \{EII.[local name], EII.[namespace]} by
deriving them from the @XmlRootElement annotation following the Java to
Schema mapping rules in chapter 8. Marshal obj instance as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_22516[See Type]”.

[#50536490_pgfId-1047434]##Goto step 4

. [#50536490_pgfId-1045963]##If obj has neither an @XmlRootElement nor
is a JAXBElement instance, then throw a _JAXBException_ and terminate
processing.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1047469]##done

==== [#50536490_pgfId-1045992]##[#50536490_22516]##Type

[#50536490_pgfId-1047807]##The type must be marshalled as follows. If
the type is an instance of

* [#50536490_pgfId-1052814]##JAXBElement , then marshal as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_59502[See JAXBElement]”.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1052836]##Otherwise, marshal the type as follows. If
the type is a :
* [#50536490_pgfId-1052881]##class, then marshal as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_32795[See class]”.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1052892]##primitive type or standard class, then
marshal as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_95261[See Primitives and
Standard classes]”
* [#50536490_pgfId-1052899]##enum type then marshal following the schema
to which it is mapped.

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1046994]##[#50536490_59502]##JAXBElement

[#50536490_pgfId-1046995]##An _obj,_ that is an instance of
_javax.xml.bind.JAXBElement_ must be marshalled as specified here:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1046996]## _JAXBElement jaxbelem = (JAXBElement)
obj;_
. [#50536490_pgfId-1046997]##set \{EII.[local name] , EII.[namespace]}
to _jaxbelem.getName()_
. [#50536490_pgfId-1046998]##if _jaxbelem.isNil()_ , add _xsi:nil_ to
EII.[attributes]
. [#50536490_pgfId-1046999]##

. [#50536490_pgfId-1052043]##if _jaxbelem.isTypeSubstituted()_ is true,
then type substitution has occurred i.e. _jaxbelem.getDeclaredType()_
(static type) is different from _jaxbelem.getValue()_ (the type of the
value for this instance). So,
. [#50536490_pgfId-1052044]##EII.[local name] = “type”
. [#50536490_pgfId-1052045]##EII.[prefix]=”xsi”
. [#50536490_pgfId-1047889]##EII.[normalized value] = QName of the
schema type to which _jaxbelem.getValue()_ is mapped following Java ->
Schema mapping rules in Chapter 8. For e.g.

[#50536490_pgfId-1047003]## <foo xsi:type=”MyAddrType”/>

. [#50536490_pgfId-1047004]##set boundType to _jaxbelem.getValue()_ if
_jaxbelem.isTypeSubstituted()_ is _true_ otherwise
_jaxbelem.getDeclaredType()_
. [#50536490_pgfId-1047005]##determine the valueType to be marshalled.
If the program element being processed is associated with
@XmlJavaTypeAdapter then boundType is

[#50536490_pgfId-1047006]## valueType =
@XmlJavaTypeAdapter.value().marshal(boundType)

[#50536490_pgfId-1047007]##otherwise valueType is boundType

. [#50536490_pgfId-1046992]##map valueType to XML infoset information
items as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_22516[See Type]” and add
them to EII.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1047911]##marshal EII.

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1046882]##[#50536490_32795]##class

[#50536490_pgfId-1045996]##A class must be mapped to XML infoset items
as follows:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1047927]##If a class mapped to a value as specified
link:jaxb.htm#50536452_24636[See @XmlValue]”, then map the value to an
XML infoset and add it to EII.[children]

[#50536490_pgfId-1047640]##return

. [#50536490_pgfId-1047493]##For each property that is mapped to XML
attribute as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536452_58593[See
@XmlAttribute]”:
. [#50536490_pgfId-1047945]##derive \{AII.[local name], AII.[prefix],
AII.[namespace] } from \{name} \{target namespace}.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1047946]##AII.[normalized value] = value of property
as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_51866[See property type]”
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048013]##add AII to EII.[attributes]

[#50536490_pgfId-1048043]##NOTE: There order in which the properties are
marshalled is not specified (XML attributes are unordered by XML
Schema).

. [#50536490_pgfId-1048044]##For each property that is mapped to an XML
element declaration, elem:
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048049]##derive \{childEII.[local name],
childEII.[prefix], childEII.[namespace] } from elem.\{name}
elem.\{target namespace}
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048083]##map property type to XML infoset items into
childEII as specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536490_51866[See property
type]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1048050]##add childEII to EII.[children]

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1047506]##[#50536490_51866]##property type

[#50536490_pgfId-1053082]##The value of a property with type ,
boundType, must be marshalled into childEII (set by “caller of this
section”) as follows:

. [#50536490_pgfId-1053083]##If property does not have a getter method
as specified in section link:jaxb.htm#50536490_98148[See
Getters/Setters]” then report a javax.xml.bind.ValidationEvent. Goto
step 4.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1053086]##If the value of the property being
marshalled is a subtype boundType, then
. [#50536490_pgfId-1053078]##EII.[local name] = “type”
. [#50536490_pgfId-1052077]##EII.[prefix]=”xsi”
. [#50536490_pgfId-1052108]##EII.[normalized value] = QName of the
schema type to which _jaxbelem.getValue()_ is mapped following Java ->
Schema mapping rules in Chapter 8. For e.g.

[#50536490_pgfId-1052109]## <foo xsi:type=”MyAddrType”/>

. [#50536490_pgfId-1052126]##add EII to childEII
. [#50536490_pgfId-1052071]##Marshal the value as specified in
link:jaxb.htm#50536490_22516[See Type]”.
. [#50536490_pgfId-1053111]##Return

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1046172]##[#50536490_95261]##Primitives and Standard classes

[#50536490_pgfId-1046019]##Primitive values and standard classes
described in this section map to XML schema simple types.

[#50536490_pgfId-1046560]##The value of a primitive type or a standard
class must be marshalled to a lexical representation or unmarshalled
from a lexical representation as specified in the below:

* [#50536490_pgfId-1046585]##using a print or parse method in
javax.xml.bind.DatatypeConverter interface:

[#50536490_pgfId-1046594]##Many of the types have a corresponding print
and parse method in javax.xml.bind.DatatypeConverter interface for
converting a value to a lexical representation in XML and vice versa.
The implementation of DatatypeConverter is JAXB Provider specific.

[#50536490_pgfId-1049140]##A XML Schema simple type can have more than
lexical representation (e.g. “true” “false” “0” “1”). Since the
DatatypeConverter implementation is JAXB Provider specific, the exact
lexical representation that a value is marshalled to can vary from one
JAXB Provider to another. However, the lexical representation must be
valid with respect to the XML Schema.

* [#50536490_pgfId-1051962]##some data types such as
XMLGregorianCalendar contain methods on the class that return or consume
their XML lexical representation. For such datatypes, the method
indicated in the table is used.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1051963]##A wrapper class (e.g. java.lang.Integer)
must be converted to its non wrapper counterpart (e.g. int) and then
marshalled.

[#50536490_pgfId-1049569]##

===== [#50536490_pgfId-1049517]##[#50536490_91068]##Null Value

[#50536490_pgfId-1052555]##A null value in Java representation can be
marshalled either as an absence of an element from an XML instance or as
_xsi:nil_ . The marshalled value depends upon the values of
_@XmlElement.required()_ and _@XmlElement.nillable()_ annotation
elements on the property/field and must be marshalled as shown below.
For clarity, example schema fragments (as determined by the mapping
rules specified in Chapter 8) for the following field

[#50536490_pgfId-1052680]##@XmlElement(required=”..”, nillable=”...”)

[#50536490_pgfId-1052958]##foo;

[#50536490_pgfId-1052679]##are reproduced here along with the XML
representation for null value produced by marshalling.

* [#50536490_pgfId-1052556]## _@XmlElement(required=true, nillable_ =
_false)_

[#50536490_pgfId-1052431]##The value of the property/field cannot be
null.

[#50536490_pgfId-1052438]## // Example: generated schema

[#50536490_pgfId-1052703]## <xs:element name=”foo” minOccurs=”1”/ ...>

[#50536490_pgfId-1052962]## ...

[#50536490_pgfId-1052961]## </xs:element>

* [#50536490_pgfId-1052704]## _@XmlElement(required=true,
nillable=true)_

[#50536490_pgfId-1052705]##null is marshalled as _xsi:nil=”true”_

[#50536490_pgfId-1052521]## // Example:generated schema

[#50536490_pgfId-1052527]## <xs:element name=”foo” minOccurs=”1”
nillable=”true” ...>

[#50536490_pgfId-1052963]## ...

[#50536490_pgfId-1052964]## /xs:element>

[#50536490_pgfId-1052757]## 

[#50536490_pgfId-1052570]## <!-- marshalled XML representation for null
value -->

[#50536490_pgfId-1052571]## <foo xsi:nil=”true” .../>

* [#50536490_pgfId-1052389]## _@XmlElement(required=false,
nillable=true)_

[#50536490_pgfId-1052572]##null is marshalled as _xsi:nil=”true”_

[#50536490_pgfId-1052752]## // Examle: generated schema

[#50536490_pgfId-1052957]## <xs:element name=”foo” minOccurs=”0” ...>

[#50536490_pgfId-1052965]## ...

[#50536490_pgfId-1052966]## </xs:element>

[#50536490_pgfId-1052756]## 

[#50536490_pgfId-1052974]## <!-- Example: marshalled XML representation
for null value -->

[#50536490_pgfId-1052588]## <foo xsi:nil=”true” .../>

* [#50536490_pgfId-1052392]## _@XmlElement(required=false,
nillable=false)_

[#50536490_pgfId-1052621]##null is not marshalled i.e it maps to absence
of an element from XML instance.

[#50536490_pgfId-1052627]## // Example: Generated schema

[#50536490_pgfId-1052637]## <xs:element name=”foo” minOccurs=”0” ...>

[#50536490_pgfId-1052967]## ...

[#50536490_pgfId-1052968]## </xs:element>

[#50536490_pgfId-1052969]## 

[#50536490_pgfId-1052638]## <!-- Example: null value for foo not
marshalled -->

== [#50536490_pgfId-1053000]##[#50536490_98148]##Getters/Setters

[#50536490_pgfId-1053247]##When _@XmlAccessType.PUBLIC_MEMBER_ or
_@XmlAccessType.PROPERTY_ is in effect for a class, then the instance of
the class is marshalled using getter/setter methods as opposed to
fields. This section outlines the constraints the must be checked at
runtime. A constraint failure is handled as specified elsewhere in the
chapter from where this section is referenced.

[#50536490_pgfId-1053249]##Unmarshalling : A property must have a setter
method if

* [#50536490_pgfId-1053292]## _@XmlAccessorType.PUBLIC_MEMBER_ or
_@XmlAccessorType.PROPERTY_ applies to the property.
* [#50536490_pgfId-1053296]##or if the property’s getter/setter method
is annotated with a mapping annotation.

[#50536490_pgfId-1053297]##The one exception to the above constraint is:
if property type is _java.util.List_ then only a getter method is
required.

* [#50536490_pgfId-1053173]##

[#50536490_pgfId-1053237]##Marshalling: A property must have a getter
method if

* [#50536490_pgfId-1053279]## _@XmlAccessType.PUBLIC_MEMBER_ or
_@XmlAccessType.PROPERTY_ applies to the class
* [#50536490_pgfId-1053285]##or if the property’s getter/setter method
is annotated with a mapping annotation.

[#50536454_pgfId-1014390]## _<xs:attribute name = "name" type =
"jaxb:javaIdentifierType">_

[#50536454_pgfId-1014391]## _<xs:annotation><xs:documentation>_

[#50536454_pgfId-1014393]## _The name attribute for [baseType] enables
more precise control over the actual base type for a JAXB property. This
customization enables specifying a more general/specialized base type
than the property's default base type. The name attribute value must be
a fully qualified Java class name. Additionally, this Java class must be
a super interface/class or subclass of the default Java base type for
the property. When the default base type is a primitive type, consider
the default Java base type to be the Java wrapper class of that
primitive type.This customization is useful to enable simple type
substitution for a JAXB property representing with too restrictive of a
default base type. It also can be used to provide stronger typing for
the binding of an element/attribute of type xs:IDREF._

[#50536454_pgfId-1014400]## _</xs:documentation></xs:annotation>_

[#50536454_pgfId-1014402]## _</xs:attribute>_

[#50536454_pgfId-1014403]## </xs:complexType>

[#50536454_pgfId-1014419]## <xs:element name = "javadoc" type =
"xs:string" minOccurs = "0"/>

[#50536454_pgfId-1014420]## </xs:sequence>

[#50536454_pgfId-1014421]## <xs:attribute name = "name" type =
"jaxb:javaIdentifierType"/>

=== [#50536475_pgfId-1005736]##[#50536475_61479]##Appendix

[#50536475_pgfId-1011065]##[#50536475_89283]##Binding XML Names to Java
Identifiers

== [#50536475_pgfId-1009909]##Overview

[#50536475_pgfId-1009911]##This section provides default mappings from:

* [#50536475_pgfId-1009915]##XML Name to Java identifier
* [#50536475_pgfId-1012844]##Model group to Java identifier
* [#50536475_pgfId-1012852]##Namespace URI to Java package name

== [#50536475_pgfId-1009910]##[#50536475_21536]##The Name to Identifier Mapping Algorithm

[#50536475_pgfId-1009728]##Java identifiers typically follow three
simple, well-known conventions:

* [#50536475_pgfId-1009729]##Class and interface names always begin with
an upper-case letter. The remaining characters are either digits,
lower-case letters, or upper-case letters. Upper-case letters within a
multi-word name serve to identify the start of each non-initial word, or
sometimes to stand for acronyms.
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009730]##Method names and components of a package
name always begin with a lower-case letter, and otherwise are exactly
like class and interface names.
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009731]##Constant names are entirely in upper case,
with each pair of words separated by the underscore character (‘_’,
\u005F, LOW LINE).

[#50536475_pgfId-1009732]##XML names, however, are much richer than Java
identifiers: They may include not only the standard Java identifier
characters but also various punctuation and special characters that are
not permitted in Java identifiers. Like most Java identifiers, most XML
names are in practice composed of more than one natural-language word.
Non-initial words within an XML name typically start with an upper-case
letter followed by a lower-case letter, as in Java language, or are
prefixed by punctuation characters, which is not usual in the Java
language and, for most punctuation characters, is in fact illegal.

[#50536475_pgfId-1009733]##In order to map an arbitrary XML name into a
Java class, method, or constant identifier, the XML name is first broken
into a _word list_ . For the purpose of constructing word lists from XML
names we use the following definitions:

* [#50536475_pgfId-1009734]##A _punctuation character_ is one of the
following:
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009735]## A hyphen (’-’, \u002D, HYPHEN-MINUS),
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009736]## A period (‘.’, \u002E, FULL STOP),
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009737]## A colon (’:’, \u003A, COLON),
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009739]## A dot (‘.’, \u00B7, MIDDLE DOT),
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009740]## \u0387, GREEK ANO TELEIA,
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009741]##\u06DD, ARABIC END OF AYAH, or
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009742]## \u06DE, ARABIC START OF RUB EL HIZB.
* [#50536475_pgfId-1014350]## An underscore (’_’, \u005F, LOW LINE) with
following exceptionlink:#pgfId-1014346[29]

[#50536475_pgfId-1009743]##These are all legal characters in XML names.

* [#50536475_pgfId-1009744]##A _letter_ is a character for which the
_Character.isLetter_ method returns _true_ , _i.e._ , a letter according
to the Unicode standard. Every letter is a legal Java identifier
character, both initial and non-initial.
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009745]##A _digit_ is a character for which the
_Character.isDigit_ method returns _true_ , _i.e._ , a digit according
to the Unicode Standard. Every digit is a legal non-initial Java
identifier character.
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009746]##A _mark_ is a character that is in none of
the previous categories but for which the
_Character.isJavaIdentifierPart_ method returns _true_ . This category
includes numeric letters, combining marks, non-spacing marks, and
ignorable control characters.

[#50536475_pgfId-1011389]##Every XML name character falls into one of
the above categories. We further divide letters into three
subcategories:

* [#50536475_pgfId-1011390]##An _upper-case letter_ is a letter for
which the _Character.isUpperCase_ method returns _true_ ,
* [#50536475_pgfId-1011391]##A _lowercase letter_ is a letter for which
the _Character.isLowerCase_ method returns _true_ , and
* [#50536475_pgfId-1011392]##All other letters are _uncased_ .

[#50536475_pgfId-1011393]##An XML name is split into a word list by
removing any leading and trailing punctuation characters and then
searching for _word breaks_ . A word break is defined by three regular
expressions: A prefix, a separator, and a suffix. The prefix matches
part of the word that precedes the break, the separator is not part of
any word, and the suffix matches part of the word that follows the
break. The word breaks are defined as:

======= [#50536475_pgfId-1011465]##[#50536475_32051]##XML Word Breaks

[#50536475_pgfId-1011396]##Prefix

[#50536475_pgfId-1011398]##Separator

[#50536475_pgfId-1011400]##Suffix

[#50536475_pgfId-1011402]##Example

{empty}[#50536475_pgfId-1011404]##[^punct]

[#50536475_pgfId-1011406]##punct+1

{empty}[#50536475_pgfId-1011408]##[^punct]

[#50536475_pgfId-1011410]##foo|--|bar

[#50536475_pgfId-1011412]##digit

[#50536475_pgfId-1011414]## 

{empty}[#50536475_pgfId-1011416]##[^ _digit_ ]

[#50536475_pgfId-1011418]##foo|22|bar

{empty}[#50536475_pgfId-1011420]##[^digit]

[#50536475_pgfId-1011422]## 

[#50536475_pgfId-1011424]##digit

[#50536475_pgfId-1011426]##foo|22

[#50536475_pgfId-1011428]##lower

[#50536475_pgfId-1011430]## 

{empty}[#50536475_pgfId-1011432]##[^lower]

[#50536475_pgfId-1011434]##foo|Bar

[#50536475_pgfId-1011436]##upper

[#50536475_pgfId-1011438]## 

[#50536475_pgfId-1011440]##upper lower

[#50536475_pgfId-1011442]##FOO|Bar

[#50536475_pgfId-1011444]##letter

[#50536475_pgfId-1011446]## 

{empty}[#50536475_pgfId-1011448]##[^letter]

[#50536475_pgfId-1011450]##Foo|\u2160

{empty}[#50536475_pgfId-1011452]##[^letter]

[#50536475_pgfId-1011454]## 

[#50536475_pgfId-1011456]##letter

[#50536475_pgfId-1011458]##\u2160|Foo

[#50536475_pgfId-1013464]##uncased

[#50536475_pgfId-1013466]## 

{empty}[#50536475_pgfId-1013468]##[^uncased]

[#50536475_pgfId-1013470]## 

{empty}[#50536475_pgfId-1013475]##[^uncased]

[#50536475_pgfId-1013477]## 

[#50536475_pgfId-1013479]##uncased

[#50536475_pgfId-1013481]## 

[#50536475_pgfId-1009817]##(The character _\u2160_ is ROMAN NUMERAL ONE,
a numeric letter.)

[#50536475_pgfId-1009818]##After splitting, if a word begins with a
lower-case character then its first character is converted to upper
case. The final result is a word list in which each word is either

* [#50536475_pgfId-1009819]##A string of upper- and lower-case letters,
the first character of which is upper case (includes underscore,’_’, for
exception case1).
* [#50536475_pgfId-1014383]##A string of digits, or
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009821]##A string of uncased letters and marks.

[#50536475_pgfId-1009822]##Given an XML name in word-list form, each of
the three types of Java identifiers is constructed as follows:

* [#50536475_pgfId-1009823]##A class or interface identifier is
constructed by concatenating the words in the list,
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009824]##A method identifier is constructed by
concatenating the words in the list. A prefix verb ( _get_ , _set_ ,
_etc._ ) is prepended to the result.
* [#50536475_pgfId-1009825]##A constant identifier is constructed by
converting each word in the list to upper case; the words are then
concatenated, separated by underscores.

[#50536475_pgfId-1009826]##This algorithm will not change an XML name
that is already a legal and conventional Java class, method, or constant
identifier, except perhaps to add an initial verb in the case of a
property access method.

[#50536475_pgfId-1014475]##To improve user experience with default
binding, the automated resolution of frequent naming collision is
specified in link:jaxb.htm#50536475_74315[See Standardized Name
Collision Resolution]“.

==== [#50536475_pgfId-1014200]##[#50536475_69379]##Collisions and conflicts

[#50536475_pgfId-1009870]##It is possible that the name-mapping
algorithm will map two distinct XML names to the same word list.These
cases will result in a _collision_ if, and only if, the same Java
identifier is constructed from the word list and is used to name two
distinct generated classes or two distinct methods or constants in the
same generated class. It is also possible if two or more namespaces are
customized to map to the same Java package, XML names that are unique
due to belonging to distinct namespaces could mapped to the same Java
Class identifier. Collisions are not permitted by the schema compiler
and are reported as errors; they may be repaired by revising XML name
within the source schema or by specifying a customized binding that maps
one of the two XML names to an alternative Java identifier.

[#50536475_pgfId-1009871]##A class name must not conflict with the
generated JAXB class, _ObjectFactory_ , link:jaxb.htm#50536473_80810[See
Java Package], that occurs in each schema-derived Java package. Method
names are forbidden to conflict with Java keywords or literals, with
methods declared in _java.lang.Object_ , or with methods declared in the
binding-framework classes. Such conflicts are reported as errors and may
be repaired by revising the appropriate schema or by specifying an
appropriate customized binding that resolves the name collision.

===== [#50536475_pgfId-1014471]##[#50536475_74315]##Standardized Name Collision Resolution

[#50536475_pgfId-1014462]##Given the frequency of an XML element or
attribute with the name “class” or “Class” resulting in a naming
collision with the inherited method _java.lang.Object.getClass()_ ,
method name mapping automatically resolves this conflict by mapping
these XML names to the java method identifier “getClazz”.

* [#50536475_pgfId-1013980]##

== [#50536475_pgfId-1013982]##[#50536475_68692]##Deriving a legal Java identifier from an enum facet value

[#50536475_pgfId-1013983]##Given that an enum facet’s value is not
restricted to an XML name, the XML Name to Java identifier algorithm is
not applicable to generating a Java identifier from an enum facet’s
value. The following algorithm maps an enum facet value to a valid Java
constant identifier name.

* [#50536475_pgfId-1014089]##For each character in enum facet value, +
copy the character to a string representation _javaId_ when
_java.lang.Character.isJavaIdentifierPart()_ is _true_ .
* [#50536475_pgfId-1014129]##To follow Java constant naming convention,
each valid lower case character must be copied as its upper case
equivalent.
* [#50536475_pgfId-1014128]##There is no derived Java constant
identifier when any of the following occur:
* [#50536475_pgfId-1014133]## _javaId.length() == 0_
* [#50536475_pgfId-1014139]##
_java.lang.Character.isJavaIdentifierStart(javaId.get(0)) == false_

== [#50536475_pgfId-1014142]##[#50536475_42957]##Deriving an identifier for a model group

[#50536475_pgfId-1009936]##XML Schema has the concept of a group of
element declarations. Occasionally, it is convenient to bind the
grouping as a Java content property or a Java value class. When a
semantically meaningful name for the group is not provided within the
source schema or via a binding declaration customization, it is
necessary to generate a Java identifier from the grouping. Below is an
algorithm to generate such an identifier.

[#50536475_pgfId-1009939]##A name is computed for an unnamed model group
by concatenating together the first 3 element declarations and/or
wildcards that occur within the model group. Each XML \{name} is mapped
to a Java identifier for a method using the XML Name to Java Identifier
Mapping algorithm. Since wildcard does not have a \{name} property, it
is represented as the Java identifier “ _Any_ ”. The Java identifiers
are concatenated together with the separator “ _And_ ” for sequence and
all compositor and “ _Or_ ” for choice compositors. For example, a
sequence of element _foo_ and element _bar_ would map to _“_ _FooAndBar_
_”_ and a choice of element _foo_ and element _bar_ maps to _“_
_FooOrBar_ _._ ” Lastly, a sequence of wildcard and element _bar_ would
map to the Java identifier _“_ _AnyAndBar_ _”_ .

====== [#50536475_pgfId-1012733]##Example:

[#50536475_pgfId-1012775]##Given XML Schema fragment:

[#50536475_pgfId-1012734]##<xs:choice> +
<xs:sequence> +
<xs:element ref="A"/> +
<xs:any processContents="strict"/> +
</xs:sequence> +
<xs:element ref="C"/>

[#50536475_pgfId-1012771]##</xs:choice>

[#50536475_pgfId-1012776]##The generated Java identifier would be
_AAndAnyOrC_ .

== [#50536475_pgfId-1009933]##[#50536475_15415]##Generating a Java package name

[#50536475_pgfId-1012787]##This section describes how to generate a
package name to hold the derived Java representation. The motivation for
specifying a default means to generate a Java package name is to
increase the chances that a schema can be processed by a schema compiler
without requiring the user to specify customizations.

[#50536475_pgfId-1012788]##If a schema has a target namespace, the next
subsection describes how to map the URI into a Java package name. If the
schema has no target namespace, there is a section that describes an
algorithm to generate a Java package name from the schema filename.

==== [#50536475_pgfId-1012783]##Mapping from a Namespace URI

[#50536475_pgfId-1009874]##An XML namespace is represented by a URI.
Since XML Namespace will be mapped to a Java package, it is necessary to
specify a default mapping from a URI to a Java package name. The URI
format is described in [RFC2396].

[#50536475_pgfId-1009876]##The following steps describe how to map a URI
to a Java package name. The example URI,
_http://www.acme.com/go/espeak.xsd_ , is used to illustrate each step.

. [#50536475_pgfId-1009877]##Remove the scheme and _":"_ part from the
beginning of the URI, if present. +
Since there is no formal syntax to identify the optional URI scheme,
restrict the schemes to be removed to case insensitive checks for
schemes “ _http_ ” and “ _urn_ ”.

[#50536475_pgfId-1011873]## _//www.acme.com/go/espeak.xsd_

. [#50536475_pgfId-1009878]##Remove the trailing file type, one of _.??_
or _.???_ or _.html_ .

[#50536475_pgfId-1011889]## _//www.acme.com/go/espeak_

. [#50536475_pgfId-1009879]##Parse the remaining string into a list of
strings using _’/’_ and _‘:’_ as separators. Treat consecutive
separators as a single separator.

[#50536475_pgfId-1011893]## _\{"www.acme.com", "go", "espeak" }_

. [#50536475_pgfId-1009880]##For each string in the list produced by
previous step, unescape each escape sequence octet.

[#50536475_pgfId-1011897]## _\{"www.acme.com", "go", "espeak" }_

. [#50536475_pgfId-1013924]##If the scheme is a “urn”, replace all
dashes, “-”, occurring in the first component with
“.”.link:#pgfId-1013929[30]
. [#50536475_pgfId-1013927]##Apply algorithm described in Section 7.7
“Unique Package Names” in [JLS] to derive a unique package name from the
potential internet domain name contained within the first component. The
internet domain name is reversed, component by component. Note that a
leading “ _www_ .” is not considered part of an internet domain name and
must be dropped.

[#50536475_pgfId-1013915]##If the first component does not contain
either one of the top-level domain names, for example, com, gov, net,
org, edu, or one of the English two-letter codes identifying countries
as specified in ISO Standard 3166, 1981, this step must be skipped.

[#50536475_pgfId-1012727]## _\{“com”, “acme”, “go”, “espeak”}_

. [#50536475_pgfId-1013553]##For each string in the list, convert each
string to be all lower case.

[#50536475_pgfId-1011925]## _\{"com”, “acme”, "go", "espeak" }_

. [#50536475_pgfId-1013510]##For each string remaining, the following
conventions are adopted from [JLS] Section 7.7, “Unique Package Names.”
. [#50536475_pgfId-1013511]##If the sting component contains a hyphen,
or any other special character not allowed in an identifier, convert it
into an underscore.
. [#50536475_pgfId-1013512]##If any of the resulting package name
components are keywords then append underscore to them.
. [#50536475_pgfId-1013531]##If any of the resulting package name
components start with a digit, or any other character that is not
allowed as an initial character of an identifier, have an underscore
prefixed to the component.

[#50536475_pgfId-1013539]## _\{"com”, “acme”, "go", "espeak" }_

. [#50536475_pgfId-1013524]##Concatenate the resultant list of strings
using _’.’_ as a separating character to produce a package name.

[#50536475_pgfId-1011932]## _Final package name: "com.acme.go.espeak"._

[#50536475_pgfId-1012904]##link:jaxb.htm#50536475_69379[See Collisions
and conflicts], specifies what to do when the above algorithm results in
an invalid Java package name.

== [#50536475_pgfId-1013551]##[#50536475_85614]##Conforming Java Identifier Algorithm

[#50536475_pgfId-1014169]##This section describes how to convert a legal
Java identifier which may not conform to Java naming conventions to a
Java identifier that conforms to the standard naming conventions.
link:jaxb.htm#50536467_37846[See Customized Name Mapping]“discusses when
this algorithm is applied to customization names.

[#50536475_pgfId-1014183]##Since a legal Java identifier is also a XML
name, this algorithm is the same as link:jaxb.htm#50536475_21536[See The
Name to Identifier Mapping Algorithm]” with the following exception:
constant names must not be mapped to a Java constant that conforms to
the Java naming convention for a constant.

=== [#50536488_pgfId-1005736]##Appendix

[#50536488_pgfId-1010075]##External Binding Declaration

== [#50536488_pgfId-1010735]##[#50536488_66586]##Example

====== [#50536488_pgfId-1010783]##Example: Consider the following schema and external binding file:

[#50536488_pgfId-1010704]##Source Schema: _A.xsd:_

[#50536488_pgfId-1010705]##<xs:schema
xmlns:xs="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema"

[#50536488_pgfId-1010994]## xmlns:ens="http://example.com/ns"

[#50536488_pgfId-1010996]## targetNamespace="http://example.com/ns"> +
<xs:complexType name="aType">

[#50536488_pgfId-1010706]## <xs:sequence>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010707]## <xs:element name="foo" type="xs:int"/>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010708]## </xs:sequence>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010709]## <xs:attribute name="bar" type="xs:int"/>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010710]## </xs:complexType>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010711]## <xs:element name="root" type="ens:aType"/>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010712]##</xs:schema>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010713]##External binding declarations file:

[#50536488_pgfId-1010714]##<jaxb:bindings
xmlns:jaxb="http://java.sun.com/xml/ns/jaxb"

[#50536488_pgfId-1010715]## xmlns:xs="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema"

[#50536488_pgfId-1010716]## version="1.0">

[#50536488_pgfId-1010718]## <jaxb:bindings schemaLocation=” _A.xsd_ ”>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010740]## <jaxb:bindings
node="//xs:complexType[@name=’aType’]”>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010752]## <jaxb:class name="customNameType"/>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010755]## <jaxb:bindings
node=”.//xs:element[@name=’foo’]”> +
<jaxb:property name="customFoo"/>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010723]## </jaxb:bindings>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010724]## <jaxb:bindings
node=”./xs:attribute[@name=’bar’]”> +
<jaxb:property name="customBar"/> +
</jaxb:bindings>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010727]## </jaxb:bindings>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010766]## </jaxb:bindings>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010767]##</jaxb:bindings>

[#50536488_pgfId-1010728]##Conceptually, the combination of the source
schema and external binding file above are the equivalent of the
following inline annotated schema.

[#50536488_pgfId-1010730]##<xs:schema
xmlns:xs="http://www.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema" +
xmlns:ens="http://example.com/ns" +
targetNamespace="http://example.com/ns"

[#50536488_pgfId-1010989]##
xmlns:jaxb="http://java.sun.com/xml/ns/jaxb" +
jaxb:version="1.0"> +
<xs:complexType name="aType"> +
_<xs:annotation> +
<xs:appinfo> +
_ _<jaxb:class name="customNameType"/> +
_ _</xs:appinfo> +
</xs:annotation> +
_ <xs:sequence> +
<xs:element name="foo" type="xs:int"> +
_<xs:annotation> +
<xs:appinfo> +
_ _<jaxb:property name="customFoo"/> +
_ _</xs:appinfo> +
</xs:annotation> +
_ </xs:element> +
</xs:sequence> +
<xs:attribute name="bar" type="xs:int"> +
_<xs:annotation> +
<xs:appinfo> +
_ _<jaxb:property name="customBar"/> +
_ _</xs:appinfo> +
</xs:annotation> +
_ </xs:attribute> +
</xs:complexType> +
<xs:element name="root" type="ens:aType"/> +
</xs:schema>

== [#50536488_pgfId-1010701]##Transformation

[#50536488_pgfId-1010700]##The intent of this section is to describe the
transformation of external binding declarations and their target schemas
into a set of schemas annotated with JAXB binding declarations. ready
for processing by a JAXB compliant schema compiler.

[#50536488_pgfId-1010206]##This transformation must be understood to
work on XML data model level. Thus, this transformation is applicable
even for those schemas which contain semantic errors.

[#50536488_pgfId-1010211]##The transformation is applied as follows:

. [#50536488_pgfId-1010811]##Gather all the top-most _<jaxb:bindings>_
elements from all the schema documents and all the external binding
files that participate in this process. _Top-most_ _<jaxb:bindings>_ are
those _<jaxb:bindings>_ elements that are either a root element in a
document or whose parent is an _<xs:appinfo>_ element. We will refer to
these trees as “external binding forest.”
. [#50536488_pgfId-1010224]##Collect all the namespaces used in the
elements inside the external binding forest, except the taxi namespace,
_"http://java.sun.com/xml/ns/jaxb”,_ and the no namespace. Allocate an
unique prefix for each of them and declare the namespace binding at all
the root _<xs:schema>_ elements of each schema documents. +
Then add a _jaxb:extensionBindingPrefix_ attribute to each _<xs:schema>_
element with all those allocated prefixes. If an _<xs:schema>_ element
already carries this attribute, prefixes are just appended to the
existing attributes. +
 +
Note: The net effect is that all “foreign” namespaces used in the
external binding forest will be automatically be considered as extension
customization declaration namespaces.
. [#50536488_pgfId-1010239]##For each _<jaxb:bindings>_ element, we
determine the “target element” that the binding declaration should be
associated with. This process proceeds in a top-down fashion as follows:
. [#50536488_pgfId-1010241]##Let _p_ be the target element of the parent
_<jaxb:bindings>_ . If it is the top most _<jaxb:bindings>_ , then let
_p_ be the < _jaxb:bindings>_ element itself.
. [#50536488_pgfId-1010652]##Identify the “target element” using
_<jaxb:bindings>_ attributes. +
(i) If the _<jaxb:bindings>_ has a _@schemaLocation_ , the value of the
attribute should be taken as an URI and be absolutized with the base URI
of the _<jaxb:bindings>_ element. Then the target element will be the
root node of the schema document identified by the absolutized URI. If
there’s no such schema document in the current input, it is an error.
Note: the root node of the schema document is not the document element.

[#50536488_pgfId-1010254]##(ii) If the _<jaxb:bindings>_ has _@node_ ,
the value of the attribute should be evaluated as an XPath 1.0
expression. The context node in this evaluation should be _p_ as we
computed in the previous step. It is an error if this evaluation results
in something other than a node set that contains exactly one element.
Then the target element will be this element.

[#50536488_pgfId-1010261]##(iii) if the _<jaxb:bindings>_ has neither
_@schemaLocation_ nor _@node_ , then the target element will be _p_ as
we computed in the previous step. Note: _<jaxb:bindings>_ elements can’t
have both _@schemaLocation_ and _@node_ at the same time.

[#50536488_pgfId-1011111]##We define the target element of a binding
declaration to be the target element of its parent _<jaxb:bindings>_
element. The only exception to this is _<jaxb:globalBindings>_ binding
declaraiton, in which case the target element will be the document
element of any one of the schema documents being compiled (such choice
is undeterministic, but the semantics of _<jaxb:globalBindings>_ is not
affected by this choice, so the end result will be the same.) It is an
error if a target element of a binding declaration doesn’t belong to the
_"http://wwww.w3.org/2001/XMLSchema"_ namespace.

. [#50536488_pgfId-1010614]##Next, for each target element of binding
declarations, if it doesn’t have any _<xs:annotation> <xs:appinfo>_ in
its children, one will be created and added as the first child of the
target. +
 +
After that, we move each binding declaration under the target node of
its parent _<jaxb:bindings>_ . Consider the first _<xs:appinfo>_ child
of the target element. The binding declaration element will be moved
under this _<xs:appinfo>_ element.

=== [#50536458_pgfId-1010008]##Appendix

== [#50536458_pgfId-1009965]##Abstract Schema Model

[#50536458_pgfId-1010015]##The following summarization abstract schema
component model has been extracted from [XSD Part 1] as a convenience
for those not familiar with XML Schema component model in understanding
the binding of XML Schema components to Java representation. One must
refer to [XSD Part 1] for the complete normative description for these
components.

==== [#50536458_pgfId-1010018]##[#50536458_94907]##Simple Type Definition Schema Component

======= [#50536458_pgfId-1012531]##Simple Type Definition Schema Components

[#50536458_pgfId-1012537]##Component

[#50536458_pgfId-1012539]##Description

[#50536458_pgfId-1012543]##\{name}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012545]##Optional. An NCName as defined by
[XML-Namespaces].

[#50536458_pgfId-1012549]##\{target namespace}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012551]##Either ·absent· or a namespace name.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012555]##\{base type definition}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012557]##A simple type definition

[#50536458_pgfId-1012561]##\{facets}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012563]##A set of constraining facets.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012567]##\{fundamental facets}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012569]##A set of fundamental facets.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012573]##\{final}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012575]##A subset of \{extension, list, restriction,
union}.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012579]##\{variety}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012581]##One of \{atomic, list, union}. Depending on
the value of \{variety}, further properties are defined as follows:

[#50536458_pgfId-1012585]## 

[#50536458_pgfId-1012587]##atomic

[#50536458_pgfId-1012588]## _\{primitive type definition}_

[#50536458_pgfId-1012590]##A built-in primitive simple type definition.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012592]## 

[#50536458_pgfId-1012594]##list

[#50536458_pgfId-1012595]## _\{item type definition}_

[#50536458_pgfId-1012597]##A simple type definition.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012599]## 

[#50536458_pgfId-1012601]##union

[#50536458_pgfId-1012602]## _\{member type definitions}_

[#50536458_pgfId-1012604]##A non-empty sequence of simple type
definitions.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012606]##\{annotation}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012608]##Optional. An annotation.

==== [#50536458_pgfId-1010021]##[#50536458_42449]##Enumeration Facet Schema Component

[#50536458_pgfId-1011946]##The actual value of the value. (Must be in

[#50536458_pgfId-1011948]##\{annotation}

==== [#50536458_pgfId-1009972]##[#50536458_82360]##Complex Type Definition Schema Component

======= [#50536458_pgfId-1012156]##Complex Type Definition Schema Components

[#50536458_pgfId-1012160]##Component

[#50536458_pgfId-1012162]##Description

[#50536458_pgfId-1012164]##\{name}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012166]##Optional. An NCName as defined by
[XML-Namespaces].

[#50536458_pgfId-1012168]##\{target namespace}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012170]##Either ·absent· or a namespace name.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012172]##\{base type definition}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012174]##Either a simple type definition or a complex
type definition.

[#50536458_pgfId-1018678]##\{scope}

[#50536458_pgfId-1018680]##Either _global_ or a complex type definition

[#50536458_pgfId-1012176]##\{derivation method}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012178]##Either extension or restriction.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012180]##\{final}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012182]##A subset of \{extension, restriction}.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012184]##\{abstract}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012186]##A boolean

[#50536458_pgfId-1012188]##\{attribute uses}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012190]##A set of attribute uses.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012192]##\{attribute wildcard}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012194]##Optional. A wildcard.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012196]##\{content type}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012198]## One of empty, a simple type definition, or a
pair consisting of a ·content model· and one of mixed, element-only.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012200]##\{prohibited substitutions}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012202]##A subset of \{extension, restriction}.

[#50536458_pgfId-1018685]##\{substitution group affiliation}

[#50536458_pgfId-1018687]##Optional. If exists, this element declaration
belongs to a substitution group and this specified element name is the
QName of the substitution head.

[#50536458_pgfId-1012478]##\{annotations}

[#50536458_pgfId-1012480]##A set of annotations.

==== [#50536458_pgfId-1009974]##[#50536458_10343]##Element Declaration Schema Component

======= [#50536458_pgfId-1012642]##Element Declaration Schema Components

[#50536458_pgfId-1012646]##Component

[#50536458_pgfId-1012648]##Description
